Tongren Fuyuan Hall Receives - A Letter from Someone Jumping into the River - Explains Clothing and Asks for Body to be Collected, the Coffin Head Inscribed with the Letters CVY 126

The Tongren Fuyuan Branch Hall at No. 6 Ningbo Road, French Concession, received a letter from the 13th Post Office at 1:00 PM yesterday. Upon opening it, it was a Western-style letter paper (the envelope was also Western-style) with white background and blue horizontal stripes, stating that the writer was committing suicide by jumping into the river and requesting the collection of the body. It was written in pencil. The original text reads, "To all the gentlemen of Tongren Fuyuan Hall, I, due to various circumstances, am committing suicide and jumping into the river because there is no other way. When I am dying, I will be wearing a gray pongee long shirt, striped cotton short shirt, ramie short pants, silk knit undershirt, dark colored short pants, gray silk socks, and white canvas shoes. If the body is found, please inscribe the letters CVY on the coffin head when you collect it, or someone may come to claim it. As I am dying, I am overwhelmed with gratitude. Sincerely yours, respectfully, and wish you peace. Signed Yongren CVY (three Western letters) final note," etc. The letter was received by the General Post Office at 11:00 AM today and sent to the 13th District Post Office on Catholic Church Street for delivery. Because there was no address on the letter, it was impossible to investigate. The director of the hall, Mr. Guo Shaowen, sent someone to deliver the letter to the Nanshi Rescue Bureau to notify the rescue boatmen to pay attention to salvaging the body on the river surface.

Landlord Sued by Tenant for Fraud and Restriction of Freedom: Dispute Over 500 Yuan Deposit, Early Morning Harassment, Forced Eviction, and Roof Removal 127

Ms. Shi Wu, a woman from Ningbo, recently hired attorney Zhang He-wo to file a complaint with the First Special Court against Li Wei-nong, the landlord of a property on Pike Road in Sui Zhi Lane, and his rental agent, Zhu Bao-sheng, accusing them of fraudulent acquisition of property and restriction of freedom. She also filed a private lawsuit seeking reimbursement of the 500 yuan deposit, 1 yuan for mental distress, and 400 yuan for decoration losses and relocation expenses. This morning, Judge Zhan Liang-ce presided over the court hearing, and both defendants, accompanied by their defense attorney Jiang Chi-ping, appeared. Ms. Shi Wu claimed that the defendant, Li Wei-nong, was the landlord of the property in Sui Zhi Lane. Last October, when the tenant of house number 21 moved out, her husband, Shi Zhi, rented the property from the defendant for a monthly rent of 78 yuan and signed a long-term lease. However, Li demanded a 500 yuan deposit as security for the rent. Her husband borrowed a check for 500 yuan from his friend Wang Sheng-he and handed it over, but no receipt was given at the time. On February 23rd of this year, she sent a double-registered letter to urge for the receipt, but the reply claimed that the 500 yuan paid was to cover the previous tenant's unpaid rent. Her husband was shocked and refuted the claim sternly. However, on May 11th, Li suddenly issued a notice stating that he was renovating the house and ordered them to move out. Her husband became ill from the shock and passed away on May 31st. In her grief, she was overwhelmed. Before she could settle the funeral arrangements and proceed with the lawsuit according to her husband's wishes, Li cut off the water supply on the morning of June 13th and instructed his rental agent, Zhu Bao-sheng, to break into her house, demanding that she move out within three days, or her furniture would be removed. She took Zhu to the Xin Zha police station and requested that he be prosecuted in court. Unsatisfied, Li returned the following afternoon with a police officer and broke into her house without cause, threatening her to move out. The roof of the house she currently occupies has been removed by the defendants. Recently, during the rainy season, the clothes and furniture are often soaked by leaks. She requested that the construction be stopped. When questioned, Li Wei-nong stated that part of the house had collapsed on March 24th of this year, injuring a child. The child's family filed a lawsuit, and he paid 5 yuan for medical expenses to settle the matter. He claimed that the house was old and dilapidated and posed a public hazard, so he ordered it to be demolished. He stated that the 500 yuan he received was paid by the plaintiff's husband on behalf of the former tenant, Wu Zhao-sheng, to cover old debts. Because Wu owed several months of rent and had secretly sublet the house to the plaintiff's husband, Shi Er-bin, he sued Wu in court and obtained a judgment ordering him to repay the old debts, but the eviction was not allowed. Subsequently, the plaintiff's husband intervened and mediated, renting the house to Shi Er-bin and having Shi pay the old debts of 500 yuan on behalf of Wu. He claimed that the money was collected by lawyer Ma Le-ming. Judge Zhan stated that the case required further investigation and adjourned the hearing.

Fire at a Lumberyard on Temple Back Road in Zhabei: Spreads to Over 200 Thatched Houses, Difficulty in Obtaining Water for Extinguishing Leads to Tragedy, Impoverished People Face the Disaster Area with Sorrowful Faces 128

Shun Tai Lumberyard, located at number 304 Temple Back Road in Zhabei, has been in business for many years. Behind it were more than two hundred thatched houses, home to about three hundred impoverished families from Jiangbei. However, as the addresses had not yet been numbered, there were no statistics. Recently, the weather had been extremely hot, and the impoverished people could not endure living in the huts, so most of them slept in the open space in front of their doors. Unexpectedly, at around 3:00 AM this morning, a fire suddenly broke out in the lumber piles of the Shun Tai Lumberyard. Due to the dry weather, the lumber, once ignited, burned as if fueled by oil. Aided by the wind, the fire spread throughout the lumberyard in no time. At the same time, sparks flew everywhere, landing on the thatched huts behind the lumberyard, causing them to catch fire as well. In an instant, the sky was filled with red light, and the fire spread in all directions. Fortunately, the impoverished people sleeping outside the huts were awakened by the fire and frantically called out to their families inside the huts to escape. They rushed to move their belongings, helping the old and carrying the young, causing chaos. The workers in the Shun Tai Lumberyard also scrambled to escape, while reporting to the police officers on duty. The report was relayed to the Ji Xiang Road Branch Police Station and the Hu Jia Mu Qiao Fire Brigade, who dispatched police officers and fire engines to control and extinguish the fire. However, there were no fire-fighting facilities in the area, so the fire brigades used hoses to draw water from the river near the Qi Mei Road Bridge. But the fire had already spread to all of the thatched huts, making it uncontrollable. Although the firefighters fought bravely, the fire was not completely extinguished until around 7:00 AM. All the thatched huts had been burned to the ground, leaving nothing behind. The impoverished people faced the disaster area with sorrowful faces. The situation was extremely tragic. At the same time, a man from Taizhou named Xia Yuan-kun, who was slow to escape, suffered burns to his left leg and was unable to move. In addition, more than ten others suffered minor injuries and were sent to the hospital for treatment after the incident. Shun Tai Lumberyard also suffered significant losses. The owner of the lumberyard was summoned to the police station on the same day to be questioned about the cause of the fire, so as to investigate the matter.

The Inside Story of a Suicide Pact in the North China Apartments: Tang Mengxia Ungratefully Seduced the Wife of a Friend, and Lian Xiao-shi Was Immoral and Ashamed of Her Two Children and Husband 129

The North China Apartments, located at number 431, the intersection of Rue Massenet and Rue des Soeurs in the French Concession, witnessed a tragic double suicide of a man and a woman on the afternoon of the previous day. Yesterday’s newspaper had provided a brief account of it. The following is a more detailed account of what happened. Lian Yao-sheng, a man from Suzhou, was 23 years old and married Xiao-shi, also from the same hometown, who was also 23 years old. They had been married for six years and had two sons: Dong-nan, who was 5 years old, and Fang-nan, who was just five months old. Lian used to work as a driver for the Da Zhong Automobile Company at number 350 Rue Lafayette in the French Concession. Recently, he had stopped working and was unemployed. He and his wife, Xiao-shi, lived at number 1125 Xiao Sha Du Road in western Shanghai. Because

something didn’t work out,

he switched to running a wonton and snack stall to make a living. When Lian was driving for the Da Zhong Automobile Company, he became close friends with Tang Mengxia (whose courtesy name was Ji-lun, and who was 22 years old), who was the company's accountant. Tang's father was a businessman in another city. His mother, Wang-shi, was 38 years old and had remarried and lived at number 61 Rue Amiral Bayle. Tang was educated and had graduated from middle school. He severed his relationship with his mother. Tang often visited his mother under the guise of being a relative, staying only for a brief moment. Tang was dismissed from his position as an accountant at Da Zhong Automobile Company for embezzling six or seven hundred yuan. He became unemployed, and his living conditions became extremely difficult. In the third month of the lunar calendar of this year, he even

went without food for two days.

With nowhere to turn, he thought of his old friend Lian Yao-sheng, who was now running a small business and doing relatively well. So, he sought refuge with Lian, asking for his help and offering to help with the business in exchange for a place to eat. He hoped that would be enough and planned to find another way out later. Lian couldn't refuse out of friendship and agreed to take him in. Tang lived and ate at Lian's house, helping Lian with the business during the day. Who knew that after a long time, Tang would become a beast in human clothing, repaying kindness with revenge. When Lian was not at home, Tang seduced Lian's wife, Xiao-shi, with flattering words and actions. Xiao-shi, being young and naive, fell into his trap, and their affair began about twenty days ago. Lian then

discovered the truth

and rebuked Tang righteously. Tang also knew that he had betrayed his friend's trust. On the ninth of this month, he resigned from Lian's house. Lian's wife, Xiao-shi, also learned that the secret had been exposed and begged her husband for forgiveness, promising to break off the relationship with Tang from then on. Lian, seeing that his wife was remorseful and that it was not appropriate to make the scandal public, let it go and instructed her to take good care of the two children and not to dwell on the past. On the eleventh, Xiao-shi took her two sons and her husband to visit her older sister's house. That night, she wanted to stay overnight at her sister's house, so Lian took their eldest son home first. However, Tang, though he had left Lian's house, was still not over it. Before leaving, he had made an appointment with Xiao-shi. So, on the evening of the eleventh, he called Xiao-shi's sister's neighbor, a coppersmith, from the Da Zhong Automobile Company, inviting

Xiao-shi out.

Xiao-shi received the message, and that night, carrying her five-month-old son, Fang-nan, she went to the Da Zhong Automobile Company to meet Tang. At 10:00 PM, they went to the North China Apartments, where Tang used the alias Wang En, and she used the alias Feng Qiu-xin, claiming to be a couple, and booked room number 15 for the night. The next day, Tang had no good plan to accommodate Xiao-shi and her children. Xiao-shi was too ashamed to go home to face her husband. The two decided to commit suicide. On the evening of the twelfth, they stayed at the apartments for one night. After Tang bought two boxes of raw opium, he first wrote two pairs of suicide notes in pencil. One was addressed to Xiao-shi's husband, Lian Yao-sheng, informing him of their suicide and apologizing. The other was addressed to the owner of the Da Zhong Automobile Company, requesting that he inform

his mother to collect the body.

After writing and mailing the letters, the two swallowed the raw opium and lay down to wait for death. At 1:00 PM on the thirteenth, they were discovered by the tea boy, but it was too late to save them. On the morning of the twelfth, Lian Yao-sheng did not see Xiao-shi return home, so he rushed to her sister's house to look for her. He learned that she had left with Lian the night before. Knowing that his wife had run away, Lian reported it to the Pu Tuo Road police station, asking them to investigate. At noon on the thirteenth, he received Tang's suicide note sent by the post office. He rushed to the North China Apartments to investigate. When he arrived at the apartments, the French police were carrying Xiao-shi onto a car to take her to Guang Ci Hospital, but she died before she could be saved. The owner of the Da Zhong Automobile Company also received

Tang's suicide note.

At this time, he went to the North China Apartments to inquire. The police learned Tang's mother's address and sent detectives to inform her. They sent the bodies of the man and woman to the Tong Ren Fu Yuan mortuary for autopsy. Yesterday, they reported to the Second Special Court. Prosecutor Wang Ren, along with forensic doctor Wei and clerk Peng, examined the bodies at noon and ascended the court. Detective Zhang Chun-sheng reported the case details. Then, Shang Xiu-feng, the tea boy of the North China Apartments, described how he discovered the bodies. Tang's mother, Wang-shi, testified that Meng-xia was her son. After he followed his father to study, he worked as an accountant at the automobile company. She had been separated from him for four or five years. He had not yet married. She now wished to

collect the body for burial.

Lian Yao-sheng also testified about how he took in Tang Mengxia and how he resigned after discovering his improper behavior. After his wife ran away, he reported it to the police. Yesterday, he received a letter and rushed to the North China Apartments. She (referring to his wife) was already dead. After questioning, the official ruled that Tang Meng (alias Wang En) and Lian Xiao-shi (alias Feng Qiu-xin) had both died of poisoning before death. The bodies were handed over to Tang Wang-shi and Lian Yao-sheng for burial. The two opium boxes, each containing some opium, were confiscated. After the examination, the two families were allowed to collect the bodies. The child left behind by Xiao-shi is currently being temporarily fostered by the police at Guang Ci Hospital. Tomorrow, he will be transferred to the Second Special Court for instructions and handed over to his father for upbringing.

Public Security Bureau Orders Subordinates to Prohibit Wearing Exposed Chests and Barebacks: Walking Along the Streets Impairs the City Appearance, Violators Will Be Punished According to the Law 130

Recently, the weather has been extremely hot, and some citizens have been wearing exposed chests and barebacks while walking along the streets to cool off. This kind of habit not only impairs the city appearance, but it is also not in accordance with hygiene. Therefore, Cai Jin-jun, the Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, specifically ordered all branch bureaus and police stations to strictly prohibit such behavior. The original order stated: “According to the report submitted by the Supervisory Office, in recent days, as the weather is gradually getting hotter, some citizens have been wearing exposed chests and barebacks while walking along the streets in order to cool off, especially various workers and rickshaw pullers. Not only is this behavior not allowed by the New Life Movement, but the police regulations also have clear laws prohibiting it. However, during my inspections, I found that the aforementioned situation exists everywhere, which is detrimental to the city's appearance, customs, and hygiene. I propose that all branch bureaus and police stations be ordered to instruct their chiefs and New Life Guidance Teams to pay close attention to guiding and prohibiting such behavior, so as to rectify customs and comply with the New Life Movement.” Based on this, it is necessary to strictly prohibit wearing exposed chests and barebacks while walking along the streets, as it impairs the city appearance. If anyone dares to deliberately violate this order, they should be punished according to the police regulations. In addition to issuing separate orders, you are hereby ordered to comply with this order and instruct your subordinates to pay close attention to guiding and prohibiting such behavior. This order is hereby issued.

Salvaged Goods from Foreign Vessel Leads to Lawsuit 131

In January of this year, the Yuan Yuan steamship, insured by the American company Mullens Insurance and the British company Public Utility Sun Insurance, was fully loaded with goods and was sailing from Luonan to Langshan waters when it encountered danger and sank. Everyone on board was rescued and survived, but the cargo drifted away completely. Afterwards, Zhu Hui-shi, Zhu Zhi-an, Zhang A-fu, Wu Niang-fa, and others hired workers to salvage three hundred loads of gypsum and twenty-eight cans of mercury from the site of the accident and sold them at a good price. This was discovered by Mullens Insurance and others, who commissioned their employee Bai Lang (a British national) as their legal representative and hired lawyer Lin Ying-qing to draft a complaint to the District Court Prosecutor's Office. After investigation, Prosecutor Li Fen concluded the case and filed a public prosecution against the defendants for the crime of embezzlement. After a public trial, the court declared its verdict: the defendants jointly embezzled the drifted goods of others and were each fined one hundred yuan. In the civil lawsuit portion, the defendants were ordered to jointly return three hundred loads of gypsum and twenty-eight cans of mercury to the American company Mullens Insurance and the British company Public Utility Sun Insurance. The defendants, dissatisfied with the verdict, legally presented their reasons and filed an appeal with the original court for a re-hearing.

The Recent Injuries of Two Policemen Injured During Arrests: Liu Junshan Still Out of Danger, Chen Yilong Is Likely to Recover 132

Police officers Liu Junshan and Chen Yilong of the Xundao Street Police Station were on duty at their posts on Zixia Road and Gao Hang Tou in the South City on the morning of the tenth of this month, around 9:00 AM, when they suddenly heard that a robbery was taking place on Yuelai Street. The police officers rushed to the scene to make arrests but the robbers preemptively shot and injured the two police officers, who were sent to the hospital for treatment. The robbers escaped without a trace, as reported in previous newspapers. It is now reported that Liu Junshan, who is being treated at the Nanyang Hospital in Xiaodongmen, suffered a gunshot wound that entered through his ribs. Doctors managed to extract the bullet from Liu's back. However, the bullet had passed through the internal organs, liver, and kidneys, making abdominal surgery difficult. As the injury was internal, the doctors found it very difficult to perform surgery. After days of careful treatment, there has been slight improvement, turning the situation from dangerous to stable. When Liu first entered the hospital, he was in pain and fainted several times due to the extreme pain. He was frequently given painkillers to help him wake up and sleep for a while. Initially, he needed more than ten injections a day. Over the past few days, his painful condition has slightly reduced, but he is still not out of danger. Chen Yilong, who is being treated at Shanghai Hospital, has injuries to his arms and legs. He is recovering every day and is likely to recover completely. He will probably be discharged from the hospital in another week. Yesterday afternoon, Chief Jin Dianyang instructed police chief Wang Zuoxian to visit Liu Junshan at Nanyang Hospital to check on his injuries and to inquire with the doctor about his progress. If there are no changes, there is generally no fear for his life. Police chief Wang comforted Liu Junshan repeatedly before leaving. He then went to Shanghai Hospital to observe Chen Yilong's injuries. Although he had three or four injuries, they were not serious. He instructed him to rest quietly and then returned to the station to report the situation to Chief Jin.

The Shanghai Pharmacists Association held its general membership meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday at its clubhouse on Tongfu Road. The meeting was to re-elect executive and supervisory committee members and to pass several important resolutions. Details as follows:

Members Present

Chu Minyi, Shen Zhongmou, Zou Jianxiong, He Xiachun, Wang Fushen, Zhang Jianqing, Zheng Jichen, Yang Fuchang, Zhang Fuzhong, Xu Wenfu, Cao Zhigong, Wu Guanmin, Wei Guijian, Zhu Hanmin, Pan Wenshun, Zhu Buqiu, Jia Yishan, Zheng Mengling, Rong Shanxian, Zhong Xinren, Zhao Mindiao, Qiu Shaobai, Shen Jing, He Zikang, Qin Zhenshan, Zhu Zhujun, Zhong Zhiqi (representative of the Bureau of Health), Mao Yun (representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters), Yu Hegui, Dai Ke'an, Zhou Mengbai, Lin Hongzao, Wang Lifu,

Chairman's Report

After performing the rituals, Chairman Chu Minyi delivered an opening speech, stating, "Science has no borders, and new medicine is a product of science. Chinese medicine has a history of thousands of years, but it has made no progress due to its conservative nature. Therefore, the mission of the members present today is very important. It goes without saying that the countries with advanced modern science have brilliant medical systems, and the health of the people is better guaranteed as a result. Many great people throughout history have engaged in medicine. Dr. Sun Yat-sen, the founder of the Republic of China, studied pharmacy in his youth. I personally hope that the Shanghai Pharmaceutical Association can gradually expand and advance to organize a national pharmaceutical association, and even further to organize a world pharmaceutical association. I have high hopes for this." Next, Cao Zhigong reported on the association's affairs, and Zhou Mengbai reported on its finances.

Representative's Speech

Mao Yun, the representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, delivered a speech, saying, "All of you present at the meeting today are pioneers in the field of new medicine in China. I am a layman when it comes to medicine, so I dare not say much. Where there is life, there must be disease, so human beings cannot escape medicine. Medicine is closely related to human health. Whether a country is prosperous and strong depends on whether its people are healthy. Without a healthy body, it is impossible to engage in revolution or any service. Our country has long been known as the 'sick man of East Asia,' which is a great shame for our nation. I hope that all the members present will work together to overcome this shame. I not only hope that the members can use their abilities to treat diseases, but also prevent and eliminate them. Shanghai occupies a leading position in the country, and the responsibilities you shoulder are a model for the new medicine field in the whole country, which is extremely important. I sincerely wish your association can grow and develop, so that the new medicine in the whole country has a model to follow." Next, Zhong Zhiqi, the representative of the Bureau of Social Affairs, delivered a speech, offering many words of encouragement. The speech was lengthy and will not be detailed here.

Newly Elected Committee Members

Executive Committee: Wu Guanmin, Cao Zhigong, Zhou Mengbai, Shen Zhongmou, Wang Fuzhong, Zhao Zhongyuan, Qiu Shaobai, Zhang Fuzhong, Liu Buqing. Alternate Executive Committee Members: Zhu Yuquan, Zheng Xun, Zou Jianxiong. Supervisory Committee: Chu Minyi, Jia Yishan, Dai Boling. Alternate Supervisory Committee Member: Ye Shuihan.

Important Resolutions Passed

(1) A resolution to increase membership dues to four yuan per year was passed. (2) A resolution to request the Bureau of Social Affairs to require all pharmacists opening pharmacies in the city to first join the association when applying for business licenses was passed. (3) A resolution that the association should request the government to formulate a law on pharmacists associations was passed. (4) A request from pharmacists Chen Yin and others to request (A) flexible licensing, and (B) whether they can join the association was resolved. The first request was accepted and handed over to the next executive committee for handling. The second request was politely rejected based on the association's constitution and the pharmacists regulations.

Incoming Letter: Preface to the Photographic Reprint of the Song Dynasty Tripitaka Treasures 149

— Ye Gongchuo

In July of the 24th year of the Republic of China, the "Song Dynasty Tripitaka Treasures" was printed, comprising 46 types of ancient Buddhist texts preserved in isolation, divided into 120 volumes, categorized into upper, middle, and lower collections, and circulated both domestically and internationally. I hereby briefly describe the cause and origin of its printing and distribution as a preface to the beginning of the volumes: Initially, the Shanghai Photographic Reprint of the Song Dynasty Tripitaka Sutra Society commissioned the monk Fancheng to seek out the Qisha edition of the Song Dynasty Tripitaka. Upon arriving at the Guangsheng Temple in Zhaocheng, Shanxi, this sutra was discovered. They were surprised by it. The yellow-papered, vermilion-axised texts were all in scroll form, abundantly filling six cabinets. They invited Xu Senzhi, a lay Buddhist from Beiping, to examine it. He identified it as the Jin Dynasty Tripitaka, which had never been recorded. More than 5,000 scrolls were extant. It originally belonged to the Taiping Xingguo Chan Temple in Kaocheng County, Suizhou. According to the inscriptions, the Dazangjing edition engraving association of Tianning Temple in Jiezhou created the carving during the Jin Dynasty Huangtong era. There were also additions during the early Yuan Dynasty. Each plate was printed on one sheet of paper, and the sheets were accumulated into scrolls, with each scroll containing from 13 to 32 sheets. The sheets contained from 22 to 31 lines, and each line contained from 14 to 27 characters. These were not consistent. Moreover, some of the sutras and commentaries that were carved were not present in the Song Dynasty Qisha Tripitaka, nor were they present in the Yuan, Ming, or Qing Dynasty Tripitakas. The volumes that were absent from the various Tripitakas were urgently photographed and reprinted to be released to the world, named the "Song Dynasty Tripitaka Treasures," to show that we do not forget its origin. Alas, our country's Buddhist texts are richly recorded, so why was this majestic and massive work, which existed in a culturally prosperous area of the Jin Dynasty, not recorded? It is like an ancient monk entering deep meditation, sitting alone amidst the clouds, wind, grass, and trees, silently not seeking to be known by others. After hundreds of years, when the time and conditions converged, it began to reveal its true appearance to people. There is probably a reason for this. Now, since its proclamation, domestic and foreign figures have continuously followed in each other's footsteps to explore Zhaocheng, with the lay Buddhist Jiang Weixin being especially diligent. The influence of this is already widespread. As for its value, it is very significant in terms of academic research, and each person should assess it based on their needs. Gu Gongchuo, therefore, further imagines that the long-hidden bright pearls of our country's Buddhism, scattered among the layers of mountains and rivers, are indeed numerous. If each person earnestly and energetically seeks them, they will surely be continuously discovered. In the future, we should compile these various editions, remove the identical parts, preserve the differences, select the good parts, and eliminate the bad parts to publish a Tripitaka of the Republic of China to greatly benefit the Dharma realm and create a permanent record. I, therefore, write this to wish for it.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 150

— (Lan Shan)

The pilots of airplanes and ships are truly admirable and lovable heroes. The sea is wide for fish to leap, and the sky is high for birds to fly. They control the lives of all the passengers, and their own lives are also in their hands. They soar in all directions, riding the long winds and breaking through myriad waves. This kind of heroic act cannot be done by those who lack courage and self-confidence. What a heavy load! What a joyous thing!

If you hope to be a good leader in the future, you must now strive to be a good follower. Similarly, if you want to be someone who is not despised by people, then do not be petty about seeking fame and reputation.

Previously, when it had not rained for a long time and the fields were cracked, people worried about the arrival of drought demons. But after several days of moldy rain and mountain floods, many places were experiencing floods. Although this can be said to be the work of heaven, the most important crux is that the usual lack of water conservancy means that there is no way to cope at this critical juncture.

Yu Xi Miscellany 151

— Mustard Seed

Li Shangyin, a poet of the Tang Dynasty, whose poems in various styles throughout the ages lament the times and wound the world, deeply understood the meaning of the Book of Songs. The Xikun style is still imitated by many today. Mustard Seed and a friend recently went to an old bookstore in the city temple and purchased a volume of Li's "Yu Xi Miscellany." The hidden words and pure phrases are a wonderful piece of writing! The book is a Jigu Pavilion edition, rarely circulated in the market. I love to extract several excerpts to fill the Spring and Autumn, and I think it will also be a pleasure for readers to read.

Good parents have no good children, a virtuous woman marries a stupid man, a family has books but cannot read them, and one goes to bed early on a bright moonlit night. This is called "injustice." Inviting distinguished guests who do not come, evil guests who come uninvited, sitting with enemies, and encountering creditors when going out. This is called "boredom." Avoiding other people's taboos, not talking much after drinking, not getting close to villains, and not arguing with fools. This is called "intelligence." Following others without asking for reasons, not distinguishing right from wrong, scolding people without explaining the reasons first, and letting sons keep birds in cages. This is called "lack of knowledge." Braving the heat to greet someone, enduring pain to cauterize with moxa, resigning from office due to old age and illness, and scolding beloved pets for the sake of a fierce wife. This is called "helplessness." A fat man in the summer months, a long journey in the heat, a leaking boat in the rain, and an evil wife in the house. This is called "unbearable." Cutting things with a dull knife, having no wine when the flowers are in bloom, the shade of trees blocking the scenery, and holding a banquet facing away from the wind in the hot months. This is called "unpleasant." Holding a fire under the moon, tethering horses to stone bamboo shoots, building a building against the mountain, and shedding tears when looking at flowers. This is called "killing the scenery." A fat man marrying a new wife, a butcher chanting scriptures, and an old man entering a flower garden. This is called "unfitting." Being able to eat coarse food when hungry, getting a small boat when traveling urgently, and stopping in a small house when it rains. This is called "not minding."

Laundress 152

— Bing Ding

In this day and age, all occupations, whether male or female, are showing a "sharpening" trend. Is it following Darwin's path of "survival of the fittest" and "natural selection?" Or is it due to the declining morals of the world and the fading hearts of people? As long as one can find a bowl of rice and earn money, there is no need to ask about the means. The ferocious faces and despicable behaviors are truly beyond words.

A few years ago, women's occupations were often mentioned in grand and eloquent articles, wasn't it reasoned and well-founded? But now, women's occupations are really hard to say.

Let's not talk about anything else, just talk about the laundresses. In our ×× building, there are at least seventy or eighty company offices. Every morning, there are more than a dozen modernly dressed young women in their teens and twenties, carrying clothes bags, twisting and turning, coming to the offices to ask if there are any clothes to wash. One leaves, and another comes. This is usually the case. However, frivolous young fellows deliberately flirt and tease with vulgar words. They even start to touch each other. The laundress also flirts and scolds, making many ugly gestures to pluck the heartstrings of the frivolous youths.

The laundress in our company is called "Old Woman" by colleagues. At first, I didn't see the laundress. I heard that her name was "Old Woman," and I imagined her to be a person with wrinkled skin and white hair, or at least someone in her forties or fifties. One day at 8:00 in the morning, I walked into the company office and saw a seventeen- or eighteen-year-old girl flirting with our colleagues. Only then did I realize that the so-called "Old Woman" was this woman. It turned out that the laundry business in our company was done by her mother-in-law. Later, because some of the business was taken away by other laundresses, some said that the old woman did not wash clean, and others said that she did not iron evenly. The old woman received a lot of criticism and suddenly understood the crux of the problem. Knowing that she was old and worthless, she had to quickly change the way she ran the laundry business. She only did the washing work at home, and her daughter-in-law took on the job of running the streets, and the business became better day by day.

Misty Records of Imperial Fragrance 153

— Originally Written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

I then told her that the color of the painting board in Jingli was too similar to the color of the flowers, which would not only fail to highlight the beauty of the flowers but also affect the painting board. I talked incessantly, not noticing the expression on her face. In fact, she did not have a smile at all at that time. But in the end, she adopted my opinion.

"Since that's the case, then place it elsewhere according to your wishes!"

Of course, I was very happy and quickly used my aesthetic vision to find a suitable place for this bottle of fresh flowers. The Empress Dowager looked at it and seemed to feel that after such a change, the color tone of the whole room was indeed much more harmonious. Although she did not praise it, she did not express any dissatisfaction. This incident passed like this.

Soon after, I had forgotten about this incident, and the Empress Dowager would certainly not remember it either. I was simply confused until the very end, when I finally realized that if this incident were strictly discussed, I would have committed a crime! How did I know this? It was because on this day—the day the Empress Dowager invited four imperial physicians to diagnose her illness—I boldly committed the same mistake for the second time, and I was reminded.

That evening, because the Empress Dowager had been dozing for an hour or two after taking medicine, the chills and fever had subsided a lot. But the rain was still falling outside, and the Empress Dowager was sitting in the palace feeling very bored. In addition, her cough was still bothering her, which made her even more annoyed. (365)

Standard Mailbox 154

— Ying Weisheng

If words are the tool for expressing thoughts and feelings, then letters are the tool for storing and releasing the tool for expressing thoughts and feelings, like a gramophone that subtly contains all kinds of rhythms interwoven with joy and sorrow. Especially for people who are alone in different places, exchanging letters and communicating their feelings is like a kind of intangible spiritual comfort.

However, in this complex society, there are too many shameless things that randomly open other people's letters like thieves who block the road. If you live upstairs, the postman's letters are often crowded. Once they are thrown downstairs, those thick-skinned people will randomly open them as if they were printed matter. Although they do not understand other people's words at all, they always bite them like little mice, regardless of whether they can eat them or not. Then, they simply throw them into the wastepaper basket like newspapers.

Damn it! If they come across a pictorial sent by someone else, they are even more like mice staring greedily, their eyes slippery and ingratiating as they answer your questions.

This, B, for the sake of friendship with A, has to consider A's relationship with C. Therefore, B cannot openly fall out with C and has to endure it. However, C is even more shameless and unscrupulous.

One's own small mailbox cannot be used, and there is not even the possibility of placing it there. Obviously, behind those ingratiating, slippery eyes, there are even more wrists that want to stir up trouble. Causing resentment is inevitable.

Heavenly principles, national laws, and human feelings are the bound-feet of the modern-day social structure network! In addition to C's lack of morality and A and B's inability to break through the network of human relations, the only compromise solution is for the postal authorities to manufacture a batch of standard mailboxes of suitable sizes to accommodate newspapers and ordinary mail, charge a reasonable cost, and distribute them near the escalators of people living upstairs in urban areas.

Little Western Paradise 155

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Sixteen: Glimpses of Tears Behind Curtains Cannot Escape Cold Eyes; Pompous Garments Meet Fortune and Chance Comes to Power

Zhiqian somewhat regretted it. People were already extremely uncomfortable, so why add another stimulus? He decided not to leave and see what would happen. After a while, he coughed twice in a very depressed manner. He picked up the handle of the teapot on the table, wanting to pour tea, and turned his face around. His head was originally lowered, so he only saw his hair, which seemed a little disheveled. He slowly raised his face, looking directly at Zhiqian. There, at the corner of his nose and eyes, were two lines of tears, rolling down the two straight, slanted lines on his cheekbones. At this time, he was not avoiding Zhiqian's gaze, but staring blankly at him, as if his countless unspeakable secrets were being expressed in his blank face and two lines of tears. Zhiqian put down the newspaper and stared blankly at him. However, this place was a thoroughfare for people coming and going from several courtyards, so there were many people passing by. When a traveler passed by, Zhiqian immediately thought that Yueying was already someone else's family member, so what right did he have to express this kind of sorrowful attitude to her? So, he pretended not to see her, pushed the newspaper to the center of the table, lowered his head, and sighed softly. Unexpectedly, Yueying saw even this extremely subtle movement very clearly. At this moment, he saw him put down the teapot with a bang, suddenly put his hands on the table, and leaned forward, resting his head on his arms. Without seeing his face, he already knew that he was about to cry. If Jia Duocai saw this and said that he was provoking his new favorite, this would not be a trivial matter. So, without daring to delay for even a second, he turned around and walked towards the backyard. (265)

Basic Knowledge

Common Sense about Household Medicines 156

— Wu Wu Sheng

We should always have medicines in our homes to prepare for the unexpected because the occurrence of illness is unpredictable. Seeking a doctor for treatment on the spot is often uneconomical. It is even more essential to have them on hand in places with poor transportation. Now, I will list some simple and commonly used medicines below:

External Medicines

1. Carbolic Acid Solution: This is a poisonous and potent medicine. It is made by mixing 98 grams of lukewarm water with 2 grams of carbolic acid. Use it for disinfecting fingers and instruments (at 30 to 50 times dilution) and for wiping injured areas (at 20 to 30 times dilution).

2. Lysol (Liquor Cresoli Saponatus): Dissolve in lukewarm water at 30 times dilution. Use the same way as above.

3. Alcohol: Mix two parts alcohol with one part clean water. It has the same effect as above.

4. Tincture of Iodine: Use for disinfection, reducing swelling, inflammation, and contusions.

5. Boric Acid Solution: Use for gargling, washing eyes, and cleaning wounds.

6. Glycerin (Glycerinum): Prevents dry lips. When mixed with five to ten times its volume of water, it can be used for enemas.

7. Zinc Sulfate Solution: Use for eye drops.

8. Olive Oil (Oleum Olivae): Use for rubbing on injuries.

9. Ammonia Water: Use for rubbing on insect bites. It is also effective for reviving someone who has fainted or has heatstroke. Smell it for the purpose.

10. Zinc Oxide: Apply to abraded skin or moist, ulcerated areas.

11. Menthol Solution: Has a miraculous effect when rubbed on for headaches, toothaches, and neuralgia.

Internal Medicines

(1) Sodium Bicarbonate: Treats chest tightness and motion sickness.

(2) Bismuth Subnitrate: Can regulate the stomach and intestines after a bowel movement.

(3) Bitter Tincture, Quinine Tincture: Medicines for stimulating appetite and strengthening the stomach.

(4) Aspirin: Treats colds, wind-heat, pain relief, and rheumatism, etc.

(5) Sodium Bromide or Potassium Bromide: Treats sedation, neurasthenia, palpitations, restlessness, insomnia, convulsions, and other ailments.

(6) Castor Oil: Treats food poisoning and suspected infantile dysentery.

(7) Sodium Chloride (Natriumoratum): Treats hemoptysis and induces vomiting.

(8) Macnin: Deworming medicine.

(9) Migraeninum: Treats headaches, reduces fever, and relieves symptoms of intoxication from smoking and alcohol.

(10) Senega: Used for cough relief.

Medical Instruments

(1) Eye wash cup

(2) Inhaler

(3) Gauze

(4) Medicated cotton

(5) Thermometer

(6) Disinfecting basin

(7) Enema syringe

(8) Measuring cup

(9) Scale

(10) Syringe (Intravenous injections should be performed by a doctor)

Age and Dosage

Generally, for infants under one year old, give 1/15 to 1/10 of the adult dose each time, and 20 milliliters per day. For children aged one to two years, give 1/8 of the adult dose each time, and 30 milliliters per day. For children aged two to three years, give 1/6 of the adult dose. For children aged three to four years, give 1/4 of the adult dose, and about 35 milliliters per day. For children aged five to seven years, give 1/3 of the adult dose, and approximately 40 milliliters per day. For children aged seven to fourteen years, give 2/3 of the adult dose each time. For children aged fourteen to twenty years, give 2/3 to 3/4 of the adult dose. For adults aged twenty to sixty years, give the full adult dose. For adults over sixty years, give 2/3 to 3/4 of the adult dose.

Precautions for Taking Medicine

Medicines prescribed by the hospital will invariably have instructions such as "30 minutes before meals" or "5 minutes after meals" written on the bottle or package. These instructions are not strictly defined. Generally, acidic medicines are best taken before meals, while medicines that irritate the stomach are best taken after meals. When the stomach is empty, medicine is easily absorbed, but for medicine that is strongly absorbed, it is best to take it after meals. Also, do not take medicine with tea. For example, the iron in medicines containing iron will be dissolved by the tea. When giving medicine to children, adding some sugar does not affect the efficacy. Other precautions: (1) Taking antipyretic medicine often harms the stomach and causes side effects, so it is not suitable to take it on an empty stomach and should be taken when the fever has subsided. (2) Taking laxatives is generally necessary due to poor gastrointestinal function and impaired secretions, so they should be taken on an empty stomach or before going to bed. (3) Taking emetics should be done with boiling water for a faster effect.

Sports News

National Games Martial Arts Rules Established and Announced (2) 157

Boxing and Weaponry Events Changed to Demonstration Matches

Other Events Still Decide Winners Through Competition

Total of Fifteen Events for Men and Eleven for Women

Articles Revised, Methods Changed

Chapter Four: Wrestling

Article 18: Competition to Determine Win or Loss in Wrestling Matches: Weight, Middleweight, and Lightweight—three weight classes. Each match consists of three rounds. Winning one round earns two points. If a round ends in a draw, each wrestler earns one point. The wrestler with the most points after three rounds wins. If the scores are tied after three rounds, a fourth round will be held to determine the winner, and so on.

Each round is limited to five minutes. However, if one wrestler is taken down, the round ends even if five minutes have not elapsed. After each round, there is a one-minute rest period before continuing to the next round.

If both wrestlers fall simultaneously, the round is considered a draw, but it counts as a completed round.

If a wrestler lacks competitive spirit and attempts to stall, the referee may issue a warning. If the wrestler does not change their approach after the warning, they may be declared the loser, awarding two points to the opponent.

A wrestler is considered to have lost if one hand or one knee touches the ground due to being thrown. If a wrestler attempts to throw their opponent but first touches the ground with a hand or knee, and it is clear that they were not thrown by their opponent, they should not be mistakenly considered to have lost. However, if the wrestler fails to throw the opponent and achieve their goal, they lose one point. If there is a foul during wrestling, it is considered a loss.

Article 19: Ranking

Wrestling matches in the men's division, weight, middleweight, and lightweight, all use an elimination system. However, to determine the top six places, the principles in Section 16 of the competition regulations will be followed. To make it easier to understand, the method of selecting the top six from the semi-finalists is explained below.

The winner of the final is undoubtedly the first place. The four losers in the semi-finals will compete against those from the same half of the draw (i.e., "A" vs. "D", "E" vs. "G"). If "D" and "E" win, then "A" and "G" are eliminated. The two winners then compete again, and the loser is the sixth place ("D"). At this point, the winner ("E") should compete against the loser from the other half (i.e., the upper half), ("B"), to determine fifth place. If "B" loses, then "B" is fifth and "E" is fourth (because "E" was already defeated by "F" from the lower half, so it can be determined as fourth). After this, only "F" and "C" need to compete in the final match, the winner is second and the loser is third. If "B" wins against "E", then "E" is fifth, and "B" will compete against "F". The loser is fourth. If "B" wins again, then "C" is second and "B" is third because they have already met in the original order and do not need to compete again. If in the "B" vs. "F" match, "F" wins, then "B" is fourth, and "F" competes with "C", the winner is second and the loser is third.

Article 20: Fouls

The following actions during wrestling are considered fouls:

(1) Striking the opponent with boxing techniques.

(2) Attacking the opponent's mouth, eyes, throat, etc., with fingers.

(3) Any action that could harm the opponent.

Article 21: Wrestling Regulations

(1) No undershirts may be worn under the wrestling uniform.

(2) Thick-soled boots or shoes may not be worn, and metal objects may not be attached to the boot soles.

(3) No objects that could harm the opponent may be used.

(4) The mat used for wrestling will be provided by the organizers and may not be brought by the wrestlers.

(5) The wrestling belt and boot laces must be tied securely before the match to prevent them from coming loose and hindering the match.

Chapter Five: Archery

Article 22: Competition Method

In archery competitions, both target archery and distance archery require each person to shoot three arrows consecutively. The top ten performers in each event will advance to the finals, where they will each shoot three arrows.

Article 23: Target for Target Archery

The target for target archery is circular, with a diameter of 66 centimeters. It is divided into three rings: an outer blue ring, a middle white ring, each 11 centimeters wide, and an inner red ring with a diameter of 22 centimeters. Each centimeter is divided into a grid, for a total of 66 grids.

The center of the target is 1.5 meters above the ground.

Article 24: Distance for Target Archery

The distance for target archery competitions is set at 30 meters.

Target Form

Article 25: Ranking

The winners of the target archery competition will be determined by the total score of the three arrows. The scoring method is as follows:

(1) Hitting the inner ring (red) scores five points.

(2) Hitting the middle ring (white) scores three points.

(3) Hitting the outer ring (blue) scores one point.

If two or more competitors have the same score, the winner will be determined by the total number of grids hit by each competitor. The grid count is calculated from the outside to the inside. The final rankings are determined by the better score of the finals and preliminary rounds. That is, if the score and grid count in the finals are not as good as in the preliminary rounds, the score and grid count from the preliminary rounds will be used.

The rankings for distance archery will be determined by the best shot of the six arrows in the finals and preliminary rounds. If two or more competitors have the same result, they will each shoot one arrow again to determine the ranking, but each person's official result will still be recorded as the original result.

Article 26: Bow Strength

The bow strength is specified as follows:

(1) For target archery, the bow strength for men is from two to four *li* (unit of force), and for women, it is from one to three *li*.

(2) For distance archery, the bow strength is from three *li* to five *li*. Those who bring their own bows and arrows may use them, but they must be inspected and approved.

Article 27: Archery Errors

Archery errors are defined as follows:

(1) Flipping the bow or losing the string.

(2) The arrow falling to the ground.

(3) Releasing the arrow accidentally.

Anyone who commits two errors will be disqualified from the competition.

Article 28: Archery Competition Regulations

(1) Archers must start and stop according to the referee's commands. Archers must not shoot before the referee has given the starting command, nor shoot after the referee has given the stopping command.

(2) The archer's front toes must be within the designated boundary line.

(3) In target archery, after three arrows have been shot, they must wait for the referee to determine the score and grid count before retrieving the arrows.

(4) After the arrows shot by the previous person have been removed from the target, the next person may begin the competition.

(5) There must be no practice shots during the competition.

(6) Before the competition, archers should check their bows and arrows and adjust their clothing to avoid hindering their movements.

(7) Once an arrow has left the string, regardless of distance or whether it hits the target, it is considered shot and cannot be retrieved and shot again.

(8) After shooting, the bows and arrows should be handed over to the administrator and not discarded at will. Those who bring their own should take them away themselves.

Chapter Six: Pellet Shooting

Article 29: Competition Method

In pellet shooting competitions, each person fires three pellets. The top ten performers will advance to the finals, where they will each fire three pellets.

Article 30: Pellet Target

The target is circular, with a diameter of 40 centimeters, divided into inner and outer rings. The outer ring is blue and 10 centimeters wide, and the inner ring is red with a diameter of 20 centimeters. It is made of metal and has bells suspended behind it so that when a pellet hits it, it makes a sound, allowing the scoring of the impact location.

Article 31: Shooting Distance

The distance for pellet shooting is set at 20 meters. (To be continued)

Education News

Historical and Geographical Evidence Confirms that Chinese Science Was Invented Early 166

Unfortunately, Later Generations Followed Old Ways and Made Mistakes

Letting Europe and America Make Rapid Progress

The National Compilation and Translation Bureau recently submitted a response to the Ministry of Education, stating that it had received a letter from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, along with a letter from the American Ohio Black-Co Auto Company to our embassy in the United States, requesting materials on aviation knowledge. The original documents were attached, requesting review and reply. After investigation, the matters requested by the original letter from the ministry concerned historical and geographical knowledge of aviation countries, such as the location of the Great Wall of China and the place of invention of kites and gunpowder. The bureau was ordered to investigate and reply on the above matters for forwarding. Upon investigation, the Great Wall of our country actually began in the Warring States period (3rd century BC). At that time, the northern borders of countries such as Qi, Zhao, Zhongshan, and Wei all built Great Walls to protect themselves. When Qin destroyed the six kingdoms, in the 33rd year of Emperor Qin Shi Huang (214 BC), the walls were connected and expanded, starting from Lintao in the west and ending at Pinghuan in the east, known as the Ten Thousand Mile Wall. After successive dynasties added repairs, the location has changed greatly. What remains today are the ruins of the Nine Border Towns of the Ming Dynasty, starting from the Yalu River in the east and ending at the Jiayu Pass in the west, divided into Liaodong, Jizhou, Xuanfu, Datong, Taiyuan, Yansui, Ningxia, Guyuan, and Gansu Nine Garrisons. Among the nine border towns, except for the Liaodong Garrison from Shanhaiguan to the Yalu River, which is outside the pass, and the Taiyuan and Guyuan Garrisons, which are inner borders and not counted, the current Great Wall should be based on the outer border from Shanhaiguan to Jiayu Pass. Its location starts from Shanhaiguan in present-day Hebei Province in the east, travels west along the northern border of Hebei Province, passes through Shimenzhai, Yanheying, Xifengkou, Malanyu, Jiangjunguan, Qiangziling, turns north, passes through Heiyuguan, then travels west again, passes through Gubeikou, Baimaguan, turns southwest, to Juyongguan, then from the east of Juyongguan, Suining, Sihaibao, travels northwest along the Heihe River, enters the border of Chahar Province, passes through Dushi, Daximen, travels south through Maying, Longmenguan, Changyukou, Qingbiankou, Wanquan, Zhangjiakou, Huanghuaping, crosses the Dongyang River and enters Shanxi Province, passes through Niantongbao, Deshengkou, and Killing Tiger Pass to Pianguan, travels along the Yellow River through Qingshuiying, Gushanbao, Shenmubao, Yulinbao, crosses the Wuding River southwest through Hengshan, Jingbianying northwest through Dingbianying into Suiyuan Province, to Yanchi, turns north, passes through Taole, crosses the Yellow River into Ningxia Province, passes through Pingluo to Zhenbeiguan, then travels south along the eastern foothills of the Alxa Mountains into Gansu Province, passes through Gulang, Jincheng, Wuwei, Minqin, Yongchang, Shandan, and Zhangye, and reaches Jiayu Pass, about 2,700 kilometers long. As for the flying kite, according to the "Mozi Lu Wen" chapter, "Gongshuzi cut bamboo and wood to make a magpie that flew and did not fall for three days" (around the 3rd century BC). Also, the "Book of Han Wang Mang Biography" states, "Some said they could fly a thousand miles a day and spy on the Xiongnu. Mang tried it, taking large bird feathers as two wings, with the head and body attached, the hair connected to guide the ring button, and could fly hundreds of steps" (around 20 AD). During the second year of Liang Jianwendi's Dabao (551 AD), Hou Jingyuan made paper kites to fly in the air to report an emergency to the outside, which was the beginning of Chinese paper kites. As for when Chinese gunpowder began and who made it, history does not record it in detail. Some say it was invented by Ma Jun of the Wei Dynasty during the Three Kingdoms period, but it was only made into firecrackers and rockets. During the Sui and Tang dynasties, gunpowder was mostly used for fireworks, as one of the miscellaneous opera skills. It was not until the Song Dynasty that gunpowder was used to make cannons as weapons. During the third year of Emperor Zhenzong Xianping of the Northern Song Dynasty (1000 AD), Tang Fu presented rockets, fireballs, and caltrops, and their use became more widespread. During the Kangding period of Emperor Renzong (1000-1041 AD), Zeng Gongliang and others were ordered to compile the "Wujing Zongyao", which contained detailed descriptions of gunpowder manufacturing methods using saltpeter, sulfur, arsenic, charcoal powder, and other materials. From this, it can be known that the invention of gunpowder must have been before the Northern Song Dynasty. During the 31st year of Emperor Gaozong Shaoxing of the Southern Song Dynasty (1162 AD), Yu Yunwen used gunpowder to make thunderbolt cannons in the Battle of Caishi. The method was to make them with paper, fill them with lime and yellow and throw them into the water, and the fire would jump out of the water, crack, and the lime would scatter as smoke to confuse the enemy's horses, greatly defeating the Jin army. This was the beginning of China's use of fire to build cannons. The West used gunpowder in war around the sixth year of Emperor Shun of the Yuan Dynasty (around 1340 AD), which was more than 200 years later than China. This is a rough outline of the location of the Great Wall and the invention of kites and gunpowder. As per the previous order, this document is respectfully submitted for review.
