Shen Bao Medicine Weekly

Overview of Medical and Health Undertakings in Taixing County 172

— Cheng Xinliang

Although Taixing is a small riverside town, located in a remote area north of the Yangtze River, it still has a population of 800,000 and 1.2 million mu of land. It is only because of the inconvenient inland transportation that few outsiders know about its contents.

Most of the people in Taixing are engaged in agriculture. Rice and cotton are produced along the river. Sorghum and soybeans are abundant in the eastern part of the city. Rice and cotton are only enough for the county's people to eat and wear. Soybeans are mostly pressed into oil for food, and the bean cakes are used to feed pigs and fertilize the fields. Sorghum is brewed into wine. Both wine and pigs are the county's major export goods.

The level of traditional culture here is quite high. During the late Qing Dynasty, thirty-six scholars were selected. People are fond of studying to become officials, and superstition is also unavoidable. However, now influenced by the new culture, everything has a renewed atmosphere.

There are currently three junior middle schools and more than 70 primary schools in the county. Therefore, many students have to leave the county to study after graduating from primary school. Now, Taixing students account for 2% of the number of students in middle schools across the country. There are also quite a few studying abroad.

As for transportation, Shanghai and Nanjing can be reached in just 12 hours. Inland highways are now actively planned and constructed. The Qipu Road (provincial road), the Koutai Road (county road), and the Tonghuangtai Road have been completed and are open to automobiles. Steamships operate on the inland rivers throughout the county, and rickshaws operate inside and outside the city. Transportation is considered convenient.

Now, let's talk about hygiene. Let's just talk about the city and its suburbs.

Modern medicine has only been around for the past 20 years, and hygiene has only been around for the past two years. There are more than 300 traditional doctors in the city. Only about a dozen are the most famous. Traditional doctors used to have a great deal of influence. Although it is now a dying ember, it is still a spent force. There are also more than a dozen modern doctors, all of whom graduated from Nantong. They have formed a doctors' association, which is very influential. Therefore, deputy doctors have gone to the countryside to practice. Most modern doctors practice privately. The most famous are Yanling Hospital, Jieshou Hospital, and Aisheng Hospital. Their businesses are doing quite well. There are more than 40 traditional medicine shops. The largest are Renyuansheng and Qingchunyü. They slaughter deer every year. There are Yanling Pharmacy, Sino-Foreign Pharmacy, and Anglo-American Pharmacy for new medicines. They all make proprietary medicines, hire pharmacists, and fill prescriptions, making a good profit. Other new medicines, such as Rendan, are sold in major foreign goods stores.

The building of the county hospital has been completed. It has not been successful because of funding and the people's lack of sufficient initiative. It has now been converted into a county opium detoxification center.

The funding for the county opium detoxification center is all allocated by the province, and the staff is also appointed by the province. It can accommodate 100 opium addicts. It is well managed, but it does not have a good relationship with the people. This is not surprising. These things are difficult to please people.

The county's health administration is still handled by the Public Security Bureau. Sanitation campaigns are held twice a year as usual. Health slogans are posted, amusement fairs are held, and health dramas such as mosquitoes and flies are performed. During the general cleaning, the county magistrate leads by example, holding a broom, and is quite serious. At this year's summer sanitation campaign, 100 copper coins were used to buy five schools of flies. There are also many health slogans posted on the streets.

There is a county vaccination bureau that provides free smallpox vaccinations for the people. There are also clinics that provide vaccinations as a side business, as well as medical relief bureaus, which are run by the Red Swastika Society, providing free diagnosis and medicine. In the summer, they distribute antidotes for heatstroke and dysentery medicine.

Modern doctors' consultation fees are 10 to 20 cents for outpatient visits and 1 to 10 yuan for house calls. Western medicine starts at 25 cents a dose. Traditional Chinese medicine doctors' consultation fees range from 100 to 500 wen for outpatient visits and 30 cents to 2 yuan for house calls. They all accept envelopes and do not have fixed consultation rates. Chinese medicine is at least 10 cents a dose. The people's belief in both sides is still balanced, so modern and traditional doctors are still at peace with each other on the surface, and there are no conflicts.

However, preventive medicine is too poor. Health education is even more out of the question. Spitting everywhere and urinating all over the alley. Who knows the importance of hygiene? Everyone knows to ask the Bodhisattva to bless them and ask the doctor for a prescription when they get sick. Where do they know the importance of health care when they are not sick? In addition to physiology and hygiene, schools do not fully understand the true meaning of hygiene.

Now, Dr. Zhou Xueyu is publishing a popular medical lecture in Taixing Minbao to enlighten the people, which is very gratifying.

The above is a general overview of medical and health affairs in Taixing. If there are any errors or omissions, I hope people in this county will point them out.

Recent Observations on Tuberculosis (Part 2) 173

— Ding Huikang

—Changes in Theory and Combined Therapy—

There are two routes for tubercle bacilli to invade the bronchial lymph nodes: (1) through the bloodstream to the lungs, causing primary aggregation; (2) the second is the lymph nodes, namely through a number of separate gland groups to reach the bronchial lymph nodes. During the age of development, the bronchial glands are most likely to store tubercle bacilli for a long time, so tubercle bacilli also mostly take this as their base camp.

The formation of inflammatory tuberculosis can be roughly divided into three categories:

(1) Tubercular Bacterial Inflammation (Lieberweister) bacillaere

(2) Tuberculous Toxic Inflammation (Poncet) toxisch

(3) Tuberculous Allergic Inflammation (Schwly) allergisch

Lieberweister's observation believes that chronic inflammatory tuberculosis is a mild form of tuberculosis infection, the cause of which is due to a small amount of tubercle bacilli, which cannot become a formal change in the tissue, so there is no formation of tuberculosis, such as adenopathy. In these symptoms, Lieberweister used hypochlorite, and tubercle bacilli could be detected in the blood.

Tuberculous toxic inflammation, French physician Poncet has published the formation of tuberculous Rheumatimus in 1897, believing that it is due to the toxin of tubercle bacilli entering the synovial fluid of the joint, causing an inflammatory state. Other conditions such as bronchitis, gastritis, and vulvitis can also occur as a result.

Tuberculous allergic inflammation is greatly related to the collapse of protein and decomposition poisoning.

If there is a bronchial lymph node, there is often invasion and absorption of tubercle bacilli. The glandular tissue collapses and causes inflammation, exudation, gangrene, or caseous degeneration. If tubercle bacilli and their toxins and various debris flow from the inside of the gland to the lymph vessels or bloodstream at the same time, and at the same time the body, or after external stimulation, becomes abnormally weak, then various defenses can collapse, and the phenomenon of disease occurs, which is the so-called tuberculous allergic inflammation.

However, the establishment of tuberculous allergic inflammation must have two causes:

(1) There must already be a tuberculous lesion in the body

(2) Protein decomposition and collapse

The phenomenon of tuberculous toxic inflammation mostly belongs to chronic. Tuberculous allergic inflammation, on the other hand, is mostly acute and special. Schwly believes that iritis, rhinitis, and laryngitis are all allergic.

Inflammatory tuberculosis, after encountering immunity in various aspects, can become a patient with stage 3 lung disease. (That is, it becomes a hidden tuberculosis patient, which is completely different from the meaning of stage 3 tuberculosis as it has always been called.)

For special drugs for tuberculosis, there is only Tuberculin (according to Koch's invention of tubercle bacilli, Tuberculin was extremely popular in tuberculosis treatment, but since the effect was not obvious, it was gradually abandoned all over the world. In recent years, it has been applied again because it can increase our antitoxin to tuberculosis.) However, great care must be taken when applying it. If there is no active lung lesion and no initial infiltration after examination by X-ray, it can be applied. For patients with tuberculous allergic inflammation, it must be applied after the toxic allergy has subsided, that is, using a denaturation method, no longer allowing it to have toxic phenomena, and reaching a normal state. Denaturation treatments, such as physical and nutritional treatments, are all. In particular, changing the environment is an important issue of denaturation treatment. As for drugs, such as calcium, arsenic, iron, etc., and especially metal salts are the most important. When they are applied in large quantities, the purpose of rapid denaturation can be achieved. (Note: Pure vitamin D does not seem to have any effect on tuberculosis, and excessive abuse is extremely harmful to the human body. Some infants have died from abuse. Some people think that vitamins should be used simultaneously in four types, or vitamin A and D, preferably with calcium and phosphorus agents at the same time, then the effect is great and the toxicity can be reduced, but the arguments are mixed and inconclusive. Only its toxicity has been completely and definitively proven, and it is still necessary to take cod liver oil and fresh fruit.)

The combined therapy of Tuberculin and metal salts is probably the most appropriate treatment method for inflammatory tuberculosis today. (Due to space limitations, the implementation of specialized surgery will be described in another article in the future.) —Sent from the Lung Disease Research Institute of the University of Hamburg, Germany.

The Dog with Pancreas Removed 174

— Yue Qi

—Medical Story Four—

Around 1890 AD, a famous doctor in Strasbourg named Naunyn was one day casually walking on a bridge in his hospital. He looked down at the courtyard below and saw many dogs, divided into two groups, separated by a fence. They were experimental subjects for a physiology professor studying the application of digestive functions. He had removed the pancreas from several dogs to observe any physiological changes. To avoid confusion, he divided the dogs into two groups: one group with the pancreas removed, and the other with the pancreas intact. The weather was warm and pleasant. Doctor Naunyn, in the mindset of both a scientist and a poet, leaned on the railing and looked down. Suddenly, he discovered a miracle: swarms of flies were densely concentrated on the urine of the group of dogs with their pancreases removed, while the urine of the other group of dogs did not have this. "The taste of these two types of urine must be different," he thought. He went down to the courtyard, collected some of the fly-infested dog urine, and took it back for chemical analysis. Indeed, he discovered that it contained sugar. He ran into the physiology professor's laboratory.

"What have you done to those dogs in the yard?" he asked the physiology professor.

"I removed the pancreas from several dogs," the professor replied.

"Then," Doctor Naunyn exclaimed, "the lack of pancreatic juice is the cause of diabetes!"

This is a story recorded in medical history about the discovery of the cause of diabetes. Sweet urine is a prominent symptom of diabetes; precisely because of this, the early medical community mostly regarded diabetes as a kidney disease. In the first decade of the AD era, Aretaeus even stated that diabetes was "the melting down of the flesh and its discharge in the urine." It was not until the aforementioned story occurred that Doctor Naunyn discovered that the cause of diabetes, with its significant symptoms of weight loss and increased urination, was not in the kidneys but in another organ. Of course, this was just the beginning of the discovery. The determination of the cause of diabetes and the success of its treatment would still depend on many subsequent experiments and discoveries.

So, how does diabetes occur? First, let's talk about normal people: starch and sugar in food, through the action of digestive juices, are converted into glucose and enter the liver through the intestines. In the liver, glucose is converted into a carbohydrate—glycogen, or animal starch. Muscle contraction requires energy, and this energy comes almost entirely from glucose. To supply glucose, the liver releases glycogen, which is then converted back into glucose in the liver or muscles. When muscles contract, glucose is burned, i.e., oxidized—it combines with oxygen brought by the blood—thereby producing heat and energy. At the same time, the glucose molecule is converted into water, carbon dioxide, and a small amount of lactic acid. The spark that ignites glucose is "isletin"—the secretion of the "Islets of Langerhans" in the pancreas. When muscles contract, the secretion of isletin from the pancreas and the secretion of glycogen from the liver are both needed simultaneously.

In the nutritional system of diabetics, all of this is the same as in normal people, except for one difference: their Islets of Langerhans are not healthy and cannot secrete isletin, or secrete too little. Therefore, the glucose entering the muscles does not burn and accumulates in the blood. The kidneys are very sensitive to excess glucose in the blood. Therefore, when glucose increases in the blood, the kidneys remove it from the blood, dissolve it with sufficient water, and excrete it in the urine. This explains why diabetes involves urine, why the kidneys are unfairly blamed for causing diabetes, and why diabetics often feel thirsty: all of this can be understood from here.

The current diabetes researcher Wooyatt says that diabetics are like a malfunctioning gasoline engine, which is quite accurate. To start the engine (to make the muscles contract), gasoline must be discharged from the fuel tank (glycogen—glucose—must be discharged from the liver) and mixed with air in the carburetor (glucose mixes with air brought by the blood), but to ignite it, the spark plug must generate a spark (the pancreas must produce isletin). If the spark plug is fouled (if the Islets of Langerhans are not healthy), then combustion is incomplete, and black smoke is emitted from the exhaust pipe (glucose is excreted in the urine).

The progress in diabetes treatment is, of course, due to a clear understanding of the nature of diabetes. Since the invention of isletin preparations, doctors have had complete confidence in treating diabetes.

Common Sense Q&A on Diseases 175

— Cheng Hanzhang

(60) Muscular Rheumatism

Q: What is muscular rheumatism?

A: It is a disease of acute or chronic muscle soreness.

Q: How does muscular rheumatism occur?

A: Many people develop this disease due to their constitution or heredity. As for external causes, such as cold and damp weather, a certain muscle suddenly becomes ill, such as "stiff neck." Also, strenuous work or trauma can also cause muscular rheumatism, such as "back pain" and "traumatic myalgia."

Q: Is muscular rheumatism related to a person's occupation?

A: Yes, it is very related. It is common among farmers, people living in the mountains, and washerwomen.

Q: What are the symptoms of this disease?

A: The symptoms of muscular rheumatism can be acute or chronic.

Q: What are the acute symptoms?

A: The acute symptoms are sudden pulling pain or tearing pain in one muscle or the muscle groups nearby. This pain is very severe and is felt even at rest; it is extremely severe during activity, making it impossible to move. Pressing hard on the middle part of the muscle is not so painful. It is more painful when exposed to cold and relieved by warmth.

Q: In acute muscular rheumatism, what are the abnormalities in the muscle itself?

A: The affected muscle is slightly swollen, and there is pain at the attachment points of the muscle, muscle sheath, and tendon. Sometimes there is spasmodic contraction. The affected part is often curved, like the lateral curvature of the waist.

Q: Which parts of the body are most prone to acute muscular rheumatism?

A: It is most prone to occur in the shoulders, head and neck, waist, chest, and head.

Q: Are there any other symptoms besides muscle symptoms in acute muscular rheumatism?

A: There may be fever, but not very high; there may also be nasal congestion, but there are no heart changes.

Q: How long does this disease usually last?

A: It can be cured in a few days, but it is easy to recur.

Q: What are the symptoms of chronic muscular rheumatism?

A: Pain migrates imperceptibly from one muscle to another, or occurs in a certain muscle group. The affected muscles have hard, contracted nodules.

Q: How can muscular rheumatism be diagnosed?

A: Because the main symptom of this disease is subjective pain in the muscles, it is easily concealed by malingerers. Attention must be paid. Objective diagnosis is very difficult.

Q: How should muscular rheumatism be treated?

A: For acute cases, drug therapy can be used, such as internal administration of salicylate preparations, atropine, and antipyrine. Apply warm compresses locally with a hot water bottle and take a steam bath to induce sweating. Apply camphor alcohol and mustard alcohol to the skin.

Q: What about chronic cases?

A: For chronic cases, local massage and hot spring therapy can be used. Steam baths are also quite effective.

Common Sense on Ear, Nose, Throat, and Eye Hygiene 176

— Tang Renjin

(55) Ozena

Ozena, also known as atrophic rhinitis, is a type of atrophic rhinitis. It is considered a special disease in nasal diseases. The nasal mucosa and turbinate bone of patients with this disease are particularly atrophic, losing their physiological state. Therefore, the nasal cavity is abnormally enlarged. Secretions easily crust and produce a severe and unpleasant odor. As for its causes, there are many theories, and no one knows for sure. There are theories of paranasal sinus empyema, bacteria, nutritional imbalance, heredity, congenital syphilis, and inferior turbinate hypertrophy. According to recent reports from doctors and my personal clinical experience, the bacterial theory seems closer to the truth. Because the pathogenic bacteria of this disease have been confirmed and "vaccines" can be made to treat it. Its effect is sometimes very certain. This disease is most common in adolescents. It is less common in young children and the elderly. It is also more common in women than in men, especially when it occurs during puberty. Another thing to note is that the nutrition of patients with this disease is generally poor. They usually appear anemic.

The onset of this disease is mostly insidious. Patients often do not know that they have this disease. It is only a slightly increased nasal discharge from the nasal cavity. After several years (i.e., until puberty), a foul odor begins to emit from the nasal cavity. The three major symptoms of this disease also occur sequentially. The so-called three major symptoms are (1) the severe odor of secretions, (2) the formation of crusts, and (3) the atrophy of the nasal mucosa. Now, they are described separately as follows.

(1) The severe odor of secretions: This symptom is the most important feature of this disease. It is called ozena because of this severe odor. Its odor is completely different from the odor of other nasal diseases (such as paranasal sinus diseases). That kind of odor is truly nauseating for three days. It is like the foul odor of a crushed stink bug or the odor of something rotting. In short, it is a disgusting, hateful, and nauseating odor. When the odor is severe, it can be smelled if you are in the same room with the patient. Therefore, patients usually do not want to set foot in social circles to avoid the humiliation of being shunned by others. However, patients themselves often do not feel the odor in their nose. This is because the olfactory nerves in the nasal cavity have lost their sense of smell after a long illness. (To be continued)

Medical Treatment for Pain (23) 177

— Li Xing

Large burns are extremely painful, and doctors must relieve the pain for the injured. When the pain is extreme, injecting morphine is the most effective way to relieve it. However, it is important to note that too much morphine should not be injected. In addition to relieving pain, morphine also causes nausea and vomiting. It must be known that burn victims must drink large amounts of fluids. If the nausea and vomiting caused by morphine prevent the victim from swallowing or cause them to vomit after swallowing, the body will not get enough water, and their life will be in danger. Therefore, it is best to inject a small amount of morphine to give the injured person some comfort and allow them to endure some pain. This is a safer approach. In addition to injecting morphine, proper treatment can also relieve most of the pain. For burns of a few inches in size, picric acid solution can be applied externally. This medicine has local analgesic, antiseptic, and protein precipitation effects and can form a temporary skin on the wound. This medicine should not be used for burns covering a large part of the body because excessive use of this medicine is toxic. For large wounds, tannic acid solution should be sprayed. The protein in the damaged area can coagulate to form a temporary skin. Nerve receptors are less stimulated, and pain can be reduced by 80% to 90%. To avoid later pain, prevent the wound from ulcerating, because if it ulcerates, the pain will be prolonged. To avoid ulceration and inflammation, wash the wound with antiseptic solution after the injury, cut away the rotten flesh, and then apply the medicine as described above.

The second major problem is avoiding life-threatening danger. With proper treatment, the dying can be brought back to life; with improper treatment, those who should not die will die. There are several major causes of life-threatening danger after severe burns. Knowing these causes and using rational treatments can reduce many of the dangers. The first major danger after burns is the large amount of serum that flows out of the wound, reducing the amount of water in the body's blood, leading to increased blood concentration. Increased blood concentration can cause blood flow to stagnate, which can lead to the victim's death. The remedies are: (1) Use the above burn treatment methods to form a temporary skin on the wound to prevent the loss of serum from the body. (2) Increase the body's water content. Supplement the water lost from the body to prevent increased blood concentration and help excrete toxins from the body. Methods to increase water content: (1) Increase fluid intake. The injured should drink more water, fruit juice, and any fluids. For severely injured people, they should drink 10 to 15 pounds of fluids in 24 hours, because severely injured bodies roughly need this much fluid. If a large amount of fluid cannot be obtained orally, intravenous injection of dextrose solution, or intramuscular injection of physiological saline solution, or rectal drip, or a combination of the above methods should be used.

The second urgent task is to reduce blood poisoning. Blood poisoning is caused by the absorption of decomposed skin and muscle proteins from the burned area into the blood. Increased toxins in the blood are enough to cause the victim's death. The first way to reduce blood poisoning is to prevent toxins from the wound from being absorbed into the blood. The above two medicines work to precipitate and destroy the decomposed toxic proteins. Once the toxic proteins are precipitated, they cannot enter the blood, thus reducing the danger. The second is to help the toxins in the blood be excreted quickly. To help with excretion, the body's fluid circulation must first be increased, and the amount of urine must be increased so that a large amount of toxins is excreted through the kidneys. The healthy skin should be kept warm, and less sweating is also good. Secondly, clearing the bowels also has considerable benefits.

The third urgent task is to resuscitate unconsciousness. The method is to inject a small amount of morphine to relieve pain and inject cardiac stimulants to save exhaustion. Keep the victim's body warm. The last important thing is to adopt scientific medical sterilization and disinfection treatment methods to avoid wound ulceration and inflammation. Note that without sterilization and disinfection treatment methods, ulceration and inflammation are very easy to occur, and ultimately may cause the victim's death.

Acute Mastitis 178

Women often develop acute mastitis during breastfeeding. This is also a very painful condition. Women who have raised children experience this kind of suffering very often. In larger hospitals, patients seeking treatment for this condition can be seen every day. The causes, prevention, pain relief, and treatment of this disease are briefly described below for the reader's reference.

Once acute mastitis occurs, the affected area will be painful. If treated properly at the onset of inflammation, the situation can be turned from danger to safety. If not treated properly, the affected area will ulcerate after acute inflammation and become chronic mastitis. The cause of acute mastitis is often that women who are not healthy and are anemic have cracked nipples or sores on their nipples, allowing bacteria to invade deep into the breast and cause acute inflammation. Pay attention to breast injury is also a very important cause. During lactation, the breasts are often heavy and sagging. If the breasts are full and you run quickly, the breasts can be injured. Even a slight collision can cause this problem. The structure of the breast is mostly fatty tissue mixed with milk cells and some connective tissue. The ability of this type of tissue to resist bacteria is very weak, so large abscesses are prone to occur, and it is also slow to heal after ulceration.

When acute mastitis starts, the inflamed area swells and is also intensely painful. The body also feels feverish and chills. Due to unbearable pain, breastfeeding is difficult, or the swelling obstructs the milk ducts, inflammation and pain are compounded by milk distension, which is adding fuel to the fire, and the patient cannot sleep or eat well. After several days of such pain, it will mostly suppurate. If treated properly at the beginning, there is a good chance that the swelling will gradually subside and the condition will be completely cured. If left to nature without seeking medical treatment, the affected area will sometimes ulcerate and the wound will not close easily.

The highest goal of treatment is to relieve pain and reduce inflammation and swelling at the same time. To achieve this goal, the pathology must be understood and rational treatment methods must be used. To relieve pain and reduce swelling at the onset of inflammation, the first urgent task is to rest the breast. Rest is also the first secret to reducing inflammation and relieving pain. It is appropriate for inflammation in any part of the body. It must be known that the position of the breast is sagging and it swings with the movement of the body at all times. If the breast is allowed to swing naturally, it will certainly not be able to rest. To make the inflamed breast rest, a very simple method is to lift the breast or wrap it with bandages so that the breast does not swing with the movement of the body. The arm on the same side as the inflamed breast should also be wrapped so that it cannot move, because when the arm moves, the muscles at the bottom of the breast will also move. If these muscles do not move, the breast can rest completely. It would certainly be even better to also rest in bed, following the above method. In addition to rest, heat, such as hot wet compresses, three times a day, is also very effective in relieving pain and reducing swelling. Applying this kind of heat to the inflamed part can dilate the blood vessels, thereby reducing the tension of inflammation, and the pain can also be reduced by more than half. By increasing blood flow, toxins can also be excreted more, and swelling also has a chance to subside sooner. Another thing that greatly helps reduce swelling and relieve pain is to periodically extract milk from the inflamed breast. The method is to use a breast pump several times a day to extract the milk so that there is no accumulation of milk in the breast. This also has a small effect on pain relief. In addition to the above methods, applying belladonna ointment to the affected area also has some benefits in reducing inflammation and relieving pain. As for the Chinese people, when an abscess occurs in the breast, they only know to apply plasters and hope to reduce inflammation and swelling. It is undoubtedly certain that such a method will not achieve satisfactory results.

Even if the above methods are implemented, abscess formation is sometimes unavoidable. When there are signs of pus in the inflammation, surgery should be performed to release the pus. After the pus is completely drained, it can gradually heal completely. Anesthetics or general anesthesia can be used during surgery to avoid pain. If you are afraid of pain and do not have surgery, the abscess will often ulcerate on its own after many days. It will not be easy to treat after ulceration, and at least you will have to suffer for several more months, and the body will also suffer great damage.

To avoid the pain of mastitis, women who breastfeed should prevent mastitis. The methods of prevention can be summarized as follows: (1) Women who breastfeed must pay attention not to injure the breast. Injuries to the breast, such as bites, bumps, hits, and rapid running, should be avoided. (2) Small sores or cracks on the breast should be treated with antiseptic methods as soon as possible to avoid causing mastitis. (3) If the breast is slightly swollen and painful, it should be treated according to the above methods.

Popular Lecture on Modern Venereology (9) 179

— Chen Shengbai (Compiled) Yin Muqiang (Proofread)

Part Two: Gonorrhea

Chapter Three: Transmission of Gonorrhea

Gonorrhea is an infectious disease. The necessary condition for its infection is the presence of the causative agent, namely gonococcus.

Gonococcus infection is mostly due to sexual intercourse between men and women. Indirect transmission through fingers, bathhouses, cloths, and other utensils is only seen in young girls whose development is not yet complete.

As for the mechanism of transmission, in men, the urethra opening widens as a result of penile erection, allowing gonococci to be transmitted along with the gonorrheal secretions. Moreover, after ejaculation during intercourse, the erected penis suddenly shrinks, thus having a pump-like effect, making it easier for gonococci to be drawn into the urethra along with the secretions.

The degree of gonococcus infection varies depending on various circumstances. Abnormal urethras, such as epispadias and hypospadias, are more susceptible than normal ones. Urination and genital washing immediately after intercourse can reduce the chance of infection. In addition, there is a relationship to individual characteristics and environment.

In women with chronic gonorrhea, there are very few gonococci in their secretions at ordinary times, and the infectivity is not very obvious. However, excessive intercourse and menstruation cause congestion of the reproductive organs, causing a rapid increase in gonococci. Therefore, it often happens that the same partner is only infected after several times. This is the reason.

Gonococcus infection initially occurs in the most anterior part of the urethra, so it is easily affected by the action of germicides. The next day, it gradually spreads to the entire urethral mucosa and deeper into the underlying tissues. At this time, the administration of germicides is less effective. Therefore, as soon as one contracts gonorrhea, one should seek treatment from a doctor. Otherwise, a spark can start a prairie fire and cannot be contained.

Chapter Four: Brief Overview of the Anatomy of Male and Female Urogenital Organs Related to Gonorrhea

To make it easier for readers to understand the course and symptoms of gonorrhea, the anatomy of the urogenital organs is briefly described as follows.

One, Male Urethra

A, External Urethral Meatus (Orifficium externum) There is an accessory urethra.

B, Navicular Fossa (Fossa naviculari) is quite wide. Its concavity is boat-shaped.

C, Corpus Spongiosum (Pars cavernosa) is the spongy tissue surrounding the urethra.

D, Bulbar Portion (Par bulosa) is the rearmost part of the corpus spongiosum of the urethra. There are numerous mucosal recesses called Morgangniscbe Lacune. In addition, there are openings of glands equally distributed in the urethral mucosa (Littresche Druesen and Cowpersche Drueesn).

E, Membranous Portion (Pars membranacea) is the narrowest part of the urethra. Its periphery has strong striated muscle fibers arranged in a circular ring, called the external sphincter (Musoulns sphincter externus).

F, Prostatic Portion (Pars Prostatica) is the widest part of the urethra. It contains the colliculus seminalis (Colliculus seminalia), prostatic sinus (Sinusptostaticus), ejaculatory duct (Ductus ejaculatoicus), and prostatic ducts (Ductus prostaticus). The posterior part of the prostate connects to the bladder, surrounded by smooth muscle, called the internal sphincter.

Economic Special

Last Year's Rice, Wheat, and Flour Transactions 181

— Liu Tang

At this time last year, the drought was worsening, and people were fearful, thinking that by this time next year, rice prices would be unimaginably high. However, although rice prices are indeed high this year, they are not as extreme as feared last year. What is the reason for this? It is impossible to seek answers everywhere, so we turn to a portion of the figures in the Customs Report to get a glimpse.

According to the investigation, the imported foreign rice last year was 7,710,610 quintals, while the previous year it was 12,954,001 quintals, a decrease of 5,243,391 quintals. In terms of value, this represents a decrease of 56%. Wheat imports were 4,649,419 quintals, while the previous year they were 10,714,634 quintals, also a decrease of 6,065,215 quintals, with a value decrease of 64%. Flour imports were 595,748 quintals, while the previous year they were 1,957,113 quintals, a decrease of 1,361,365 quintals, with a value decrease of 74%. The reasons for this decrease are: (1) It should be recognized that before June of last year, rice-producing provinces were still sending urgent telegrams to discuss measures to alleviate the problem of low grain prices harming farmers, indicating that the food supply seemed to be excessive rather than insufficient. (2) Although there was a drought last year, its impact should be felt this year, as the food supply for that year, like the previous two years, was abundant, so there should not have been any shortage. (3) Although there was a drought last year, the harvest in the north was still good, and even in the south, such as Wenzhou and Haicheng in Zhejiang, as well as various places in Fujian and Guangdong, there were reports of good harvests. The harvest from the polder fields in the Dongting Lake area was also quite good. Jiangsu, except for a very few counties that were severely affected, also had an autumn harvest. The province that was most severely affected was Zhejiang, with 72 out of 75 counties experiencing disaster, followed by southern Anhui. (4) The prices of agricultural products have been falling for years. Farmers' economies are extremely depleted, and they often cannot even afford to eat. Sweet potatoes are now the best food for farmers, and the situation of those who eat worse is unimaginable. Therefore, how could the sales of rice, wheat, and flour not decrease? (5) Since the import tariffs on rice, wheat, and flour were increased on December 16th of the previous year, this also had a minor effect on the decrease in imports. However, its effect was still small, as it is clear that foreign rice would still be imported regardless of how low grain prices in our country are.

Looking further at the content of last year's imported rice, wheat, and flour, almost all of the rice came from Siam and Annam. Of the 7,710,000 quintals of imported rice, 3,450,000 quintals were Siamese rice and 3,342,000 quintals were Annamese rice. The rest came from Japan and Korea, with the 640,000 quintals imported from Burma being the largest. A total of 4,649,000 quintals of wheat were imported. American wheat accounted for 3,086,000 quintals. Of this number, excluding 181,000 quintals that were ordered by merchants, the rest were imported through cotton and wheat loans. In addition, the wheat harvest in the Jianghuai area was abundant, resulting in a significant decrease in the import of Australian and Argentinian wheat. Argentinian wheat imports were 1,344,000 quintals in the previous year, but only 970,000 quintals last year. The decrease in Australian wheat was even greater, from 8,395,000 quintals in the previous year to only 430,000 quintals last year. Most of the flour also came from the United States, with 355,000 quintals, some of which were also from loans. Canadian flour accounted for 109,000 quintals, Australian flour for 119,000 quintals, and Japanese flour for 9,800 quintals. The total amount of rice exported overseas was 68,289 quintals, of which 46,000 quintals were transported to the Kwantung Leased Territory and 14,000 quintals to Hong Kong. In addition, Japan, the United States, and the United Kingdom each received one or two thousand quintals. The amount of wheat transported abroad was 132,664 quintals, with 122,977 quintals transported to Japan. Of the 64,572 quintals of flour transported overseas, over 50,000 quintals were transported to the Kwantung Leased Territory, with the rest going to the Philippines and Hong Kong. A table is provided below (all units in the tables are quintals, the old Customs tael, one hundred catties, equals 0.605 quintals).

Table of Rice, Wheat, and Flour Imports and Exports in the Republic of China, 23rd Year

The above is only an outline, and it does not clearly show where these large quantities of imported food were sold. Furthermore, it does not show what the situation of domestic grain circulation is. Although the Customs Report lists some national grain production figures, it is impossible to estimate what percentage they represent. However, the amounts transported by ship are generally included, which is more reliable than simply making conjectures. Therefore, they have been classified, reorganized, and compiled again to obtain the following three tables for rice, wheat, and flour. With these three tables, we can get a better impression of the food supply and demand in each region, and it is not difficult to determine whether there is a surplus or a shortage. Looking at the tables, it is clear that the amount of domestic rice falls far short of meeting domestic needs. As for wheat, the abundant harvest in Jiangbei last year is indeed a fact. It is important to know that most of the wheat from Jiangbei and northern Anhui is transported by cart, but the amount exported from Zhenjiang and Nanjing alone was 543,000 quintals, and from Wuhu, it was 152,000 quintals, so the scale of its exports can be seen. However, this is still far from meeting domestic needs. As for flour, domestic mills have a large influence, and foreign flour is insignificant. In Shanghai, the export of flour from domestic mills last year was already 5,627,000 quintals, while the import to the Hebei region was 3,029,000 quintals. It can be said that the imported foreign flour last year was sold in Shanghai and Guangdong, and very little elsewhere. Since the machine-made flour industry closed down, they have suddenly become prominent, if they can be well managed, why should there still be imports of foreign flour! The three tables are listed below:

1. Rice

2. Wheat

3. Flour

This article cannot discuss much, as it is not permitted by the nature of this publication. However, it must be stated that the "last year" mentioned in the article refers to the 23rd year of the Republic of China, and the "previous year" refers to the 22nd year of the Republic of China. Furthermore, when using Customs figures as research material, changes in transportation methods, such as the increasing development of railways and highways, mean that more and more goods are not passing through Customs. Therefore, how to ensure that researchers have relatively sufficient and reliable figures is what we hope from those responsible.

World Gold Production and Gold Reserves 182

— Yao Fangren

Before 1931, the gold standard was widely implemented in various countries and was almost the sole representative of gold for monetary use. Today, under the premise of stabilizing currencies, the idea of restoring the gold standard is once again welcomed by economists. The definitive answer to this question is, of course, not simple; however, understanding the basis for rebuilding the gold standard depends on the extent of efforts to establish new parities for various currencies. If the gold content of the gold pound, gold dollar, and franc was 60% or 50% of what it was before 1931, then the monetary price of a fixed amount of gold would inevitably increase proportionally; also, if the central bank's gold reserve ratio is reduced from 40% to 25%, the price of the gold reserve amount will increase even further. There are several points that are unclear here, that is, how much gold will be held in the future, or how much will actually be held as a gold reserve within a certain limit, no one dares to predict, as this will vary depending on the intentions of each country.

The Gold Bloc and the Sterling Bloc

We must first examine the actual amount of gold used for monetary purposes and its distribution. The fifth annual report of the Bank for International Settlements can provide us with some information on this point. The report divides the world's currency situation into two camps: the Gold Bloc and the Sterling Bloc. The former, in addition to France, the Netherlands, Italy, Poland, and Switzerland, also includes Albania, Belgium, Bulgaria, Cuba, Czechoslovakia, Danzig, Germany, Greece, Yugoslavia, Latvia, Lithuania, Mexico, Romania, Spain, Turkey, the United States of America, and Uruguay. The latter includes Argentina, Australia, Bolivia, Brazil, Colombia, Denmark, Egypt, Estonia, Finland, the United Kingdom, India , the Irish Free State, Japan, Norway, New Zealand, Paraguay, Portugal, Siam , the Straits Settlements,Sweden, the South African Federation, and British colonies. Originally, the countries of the Gold Bloc did not necessarily completely lock down their currencies, and there was a very significant distinction between them and the countries of the Sterling Bloc. This classification is only for ease of description.

The Supply of Gold

Next, let's examine the issue of gold supply. Since 1929, both the gold pound and the gold dollar have been stimulated by falling prices. At the same time, with the increase in gold production in Canada and Soviet Russia, the world gold production has increased sharply as shown in the table below (unit: thousands of ounces):

Year Main Force South Africa Pound US Canada Soviet Russia Other Countries Total

1920 10,422 2,208 1,928 1,085 3,952 19,585

1929 10,716 2,286 2,102 1,434 4,184 20,722

1931 10,878 2,396 2,694 1,701 4,701 22,370

1932 11,559 2,449 3,044 1,990 5,185 24,227

1933 11,014 2,537 2,944 2,816 6,062 25,378

1934 10,480 2,916 2,964 4,224 6,532 27,107

Most of the increase in production in "Other Countries" in the table above can be attributed to Australia. In terms of price, the value of gold production in 1934 was 2,904 million Swiss francs. In addition, "hoarded gold" from countries in the Far East also flowed out at the same time. The estimated amount is shown in the following table (unit: million Swiss francs):

Year India China Hong Kong Total

1931 477 54 63 594

1932 1,014 28 59 1,191

1933 633 74 100 827

1934 1,003 54 68 825

Total 2,847 300 290 3,437

The outflow of gold gradually decreased after 1931; however, the outflow of gold in the past four years far exceeded the total amount of gold produced worldwide in the entire year. The Bank for International Settlements included the amount of gold recovered from industrial use in the United States, Italy, and the United Kingdom in its calculations; thus, it could only assume that all of the newly produced gold and the outflow of gold from privately held hoards in the countries of the Far East was sufficient to serve as gold reserves and all of Europe's "new private hoards."

The Demand for Gold Used in Currency

The annual report also mentioned the demand for gold used in currency. In 1934, the amount of newly produced gold was approximately 2,904 million Swiss francs, and the outflow of gold from hoards in countries of the Far East was 875 million Swiss francs (this amount differs from the previous table by 50 million Swiss francs, which was not explained in the annual report). The amount available for currency reserves was approximately 3,779 million Swiss francs or more. In contrast, the "publicly announced" gold reserves of 50 countries was 4,834 million Swiss francs, exceeding the supply by more than 55 million Swiss francs. Part of this difference is due to various exchange rate balances that were not "publicly announced," especially part of the Anglo-American exchange rate fund in 1934, which was erased.

The Distribution of Gold

Regarding the issue of gold distribution, the holdings of major countries are shown in the following table: (unit: million Swiss francs)

Country End of December 1933 End of December 1934 End of March 1935 Change in 1934 Change in the First Quarter of 1935

In 1934, France's gold holdings increased, mainly due to inflows from Gold Bloc countries. In the first quarter of this year, France's holdings also increased slightly, while those of the entire bloc decreased again. However, the Bank of France's gold reserves have decreased by 1.1 billion Swiss francs since the end of March of this year, while the United States has seen a significant increase. France and the United States now hold approximately two-thirds of the world's publicly announced monetary gold.

The Meaning of Public Announcement

The restriction of "announcing it publicly" is necessary at present. There are two reasons for this. First, the exact amount of the exchange rate balance funds of the United Kingdom, the United States, and other countries is unknown to outsiders. The annual report only mentions that the British and American exchange rate balance funds made huge purchases in 1933. The previous year's report stated that the amount received from private hoards was approximately 3.12 billion Swiss francs, while this year's report states that the amount obtained from the exchange rate balance fund was roughly the same as the 3 billion Swiss francs from private hoards. However, in 1934, the amount of the United Kingdom's balance fund gradually decreased. Part of this was due to the increase in funds flowing out of London, and part of the outflow of funds from the United Kingdom was used to pay for international loans to the Sterling Bloc.

The second reason for using the term "public announcement" is the existence of private hoards. These private hoards are not only sufficient to cause panic, but also create extreme difficulties in the global distribution of gold, making it impossible to calculate. Large companies that have to use gold dollars and gold pounds to do business are worried about the sharp fall in exchange rates and hold gold. Therefore, gold is still the most authoritative factor in determining exchange rate fluctuations today. Although some of the privately hoarded gold is analyzed and actually used as funds for international trade, this is an exception and is not often seen in the usual situation.

The Amount of Privately Hoarded Gold

The Bank for International Settlements annual report estimated the amount of privately hoarded gold at the end of 1934. The total amount of newly produced gold and gold flowing out of Far Eastern countries from 1930 to the end of 1934 was over 15 billion Swiss francs. During this period, the world's gold reserves increased by approximately 10 billion Swiss francs. After studying the withdrawal of gold coins, the consumption of gold for industrial use, the purchase of exchange rate balance funds, and the private hoards before 1931, the amount of private hoards at the end of 1934 can be estimated at 7 billion Swiss francs, of which 1.8 billion Swiss francs belonged to the Bank of England's gold reserves, while the rest is unknown. Most of it probably belongs to the exchange rate balance fund, or has been recorded in the accounts of foreign central banks. Approximately half of these privately hoarded gold holdings, excluding the privately hoarded amounts in India, China, and Egypt, are kept in London. In the United States, this large amount of privately hoarded gold is withdrawn and used as gold reserves. If the currency stabilizes and the market is stable, then a portion of the private hoards can flow out and become the reserves of the central bank. Therefore, this point can be determined by itself, and this fact means that it is possible to avoid the panic of a future shortage of gold for monetary use.

The Redistribution of Gold

Furthermore, regarding the redistribution of gold, the United Kingdom and the United States still hold the vast majority of the world's monetary gold. First, privately hoarded gold will flow into the weaker central banks, because most of the privately hoarded gold flowed out from there in the first place. Whether those weaker central banks can continue to keep it is another question. This depends entirely on currency stability and the method of rebuilding the gold standard. If the currencies of various countries reach equilibrium at the same time, then international commerce, investment, and finance will return to ease, and countries will naturally need that private gold to maintain gold reserves. If this condition is met, then the hoarded gold in various places can still flow to financial centers, and for another part of the gold, it will lose considerable activity. Sooner or later, the newest type of gold standard will be abandoned.

Securities Securities Rely on Sustaining Power 184

Last week (July 8th to 13th), the volatility of securities on the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange remained rampant. Initially, under the dual constraints of the current situation and tight money, it struggled to rise, further causing physical goods to flood the market and a significant decline in prices. The June 23rd contracts even fell below the 60 yuan mark, and the June 22nd contracts also fell below the 50 yuan mark. The discounts on various bonds had fallen to 50-60%, even 70% of their face value. Since the prosperity or decline of the bond market is of great importance, how could one cause such self-inflicted harm? Therefore, efforts were made to support the market and promote favorable propaganda for the long positions. Moreover, the rumor of actual delivery posed a great threat to the short positions, shaking their lines and causing a sudden rebound. The price declines finally came to an end. The 96 Public Bonds maintained their original state at the beginning of last week. In the last two days of the week, however, large investors suddenly purchased them eagerly, and the market price soared. It once broke through the 10 yuan mark. Although it slightly declined afterwards due to some selling pressure, it soon recovered and flourished. It is rumored that the bond is being manipulated by powerful forces, as they have been absorbing it relentlessly since last month's settlement. Their strong financial backing is evident. Other bonds fell by 3-5 jiao to 1.2 yuan each, except for the recent June 20th and June 23rd contracts, which rose by 1-2 jiao. The 96 bonds rose by 0.5 to 0.8 yuan.
