Free Talk

Cha'an Short Stories 187

— Han Feng

—Some Textual Researches on Novels

In late May, a Hangzhou bookseller came to Shanghai to sell a large number of old books. Da Jie and I were particularly fond of "Cha'an Short Stories." I was already so poor that I couldn't afford to live, so I didn't dare to think about this rare book at all. Da Jie was also struggling financially, and he flipped through the book several times, shaking his head and sighing, feeling unable to buy it. A few days later, I met Da Jie again, and he happily told me that he had finally bought the book because the bookseller had agreed to a payment plan. And I, therefore, had the opportunity to read it and write this short essay about it.

"Cha'an Short Stories" is very rare, consisting of 41 volumes, written by Lai Sixing. It is a classified collection of textual researches, which can also be said to be notes. It was published in the Xinwei year of Chongzhen. In his preface, Bozi said that the book began in the Gui Si year of Wanli and was completed in Xinwei, taking nearly forty years, and was revised five times before completion. Its content "ranges from astronomy, geography, national affairs, anecdotes, military affairs, and criminal law, to crowns, attire, surnames, given names, funeral rites, music, interpretations of plants, trees, birds, animals, and foreign tribes." There are about a thousand items in total.

Some of them are a waste of effort, such as the "Horse" section, which compiles all the names of horses owned by famous people since the Yellow Emperor, and the "Dog" section, which lists countless dog names from ancient times. A lot of time was spent, but it is meaningless. However, most of it is a good source of information and contains a lot of valuable material. My recent interest has been focused on novels. Here, I just want to say a few words about the sections related to characters in novels.

The most important part of the novel research is the "Zhang Shun" entry. This has a great relationship with "Water Margin." The text is: "In Water Margin, there is Zhang Shun, nicknamed 'White Streak in the Waves,' who is good at swimming and is considered a naval commander. Guixin Miscellany: During the siege of Xiangyang and Fancheng, the isolated city was besieged for three or four years. Zhang Hanmo defended Fancheng and offered a large reward to recruit brave warriors, obtaining 3,000 fierce men. After searching for a general for a long time, he obtained Zhang Shun and Zhang Gui, officials of the Ministry of War, known as the Great General Zhang and Little General Zhang, whose wisdom and courage were always admired by the armies. First, they established a strong camp at Zhongshuiyu in the upper reaches of Junzhou, built water哨, and used a hundred light boats, each with thirty men. Each boat was given a bag of salt and two hundred bolts of cloth, and they were ordered: 'This journey is only about death. If it is not your true desire, leave quickly, and do not ruin my affairs.' Everyone was grateful and angry, riding the wind and waves, and directly attacked the enemy's 重园, and the rebel soldiers were all defeated. The people in Xiangcheng heard that help had arrived, and their courage was a hundred times greater. When the army was collected, Zhang Shun was lost. After several days, a floating corpse floated upstream, wearing armor and holding a bow and arrow, directly reaching the floating bridge. Upon inspection, it was Zhang Shun. He had four spear wounds and six arrows in his body, and his anger was as vivid as life. The army was surprised and thought he was a god, and built a temple to worship him. Zhang Gui was later captured and died unyielding. Lü Wenhuan built a double temple for them. According to Bi Xunyuan, Zhang Shun was indeed good at swimming, but he was not a person from the Xuanhe period. Now, in Wulin, inside Yongjin Gate, there is a temple to General Jinhua, Cao Guo, a person from the Later Tang Dynasty, who was the magistrate of Jinhua. After pacifying the rebels, Wu Yue entrusted him with national affairs, and he dredged three pools in the city corner, drawing lake water into the city. Wang Gui praised him and titled it 'Yongjin.' When Gao died, the people of the county worshiped him, calling him General Jinhua, mistaking him for Zhang Shun. Water Margin says that Song Jiang went to Li Shishi's house, and the Daoist Emperor arrived, hiding under the bed. This is Zhou Chengmei's affair, as seen in Zhang Duanyi's Precious Ear Collection." This shows the origins of Zhang Shun's brothers in Water Margin, and the basis for the fact that Song Jiang went to Li Shishi's house. The composition of the Water Margin characters is actually taken from the Three Dynasties.

The second is "Han Xiang," namely Han Xiangzi in the Eight Immortals. The author quotes from the Collected Works of Changli, Qing Suo High Talks, Gleanings from Immortal Biographies, and Youyang Miscellany, to recount Han Xiang's anecdotes, which are mostly similar. However, it is said that Xiang is Changli's "distant cousin," and some say he is a "nephew," which is not consistent. Qing Suo High Talks says: "Xiang's name is Qingfu, and he is Duke's nephew. He was dissolute and did not dominate. Duke encouraged him to study, but he smiled and wrote a poem with the line 'Able to open flowers in an instant.' Duke said, 'Can you steal creation to open flowers?' Xiang then piled up soil and covered a pot. After a long time, he said, 'The flowers have bloomed.' He lifted the pot, and there were two green flowers with small gold characters on the leaves, which read 'Clouds cross the Qinling Mountains.' Xiang said: 'Things can be tested over time.' Duke was later demoted to Chaozhou. On the way, a person came through the snow, who was Xiang. Xiang said: 'Do you remember the flower lines?' Duke asked the place name, which was Languan. He sighed again and again, and then composed a poem, without mentioning that Xiang was his nephew or grandson." Gleanings from Immortal Biographies says that he can dye flower colors, and Youyang Miscellany also says the same. Youyang Miscellany describes his dyeing flower process: "He erected a screen at a right angle to cover the peony bushes, preventing people from peeping. He dug holes on all four sides, deep to the roots, wide enough for a person to sit, and only brought purple ore, light powder, and vermilion, and treated the roots every evening for seven months, then filled the holes." This is more reasonable. The Collected Works of Changli only used the poem "Zuo Xun Arrives at Languan to Show Nephew and Grandson Xiang" to mention Han Xiang. The Ming edition of the book "Han Xiangzi" has not been seen, and it is unknown whether it mentioned this matter.

Another "Liang Shanbo and Zhu Yingtai" short study says: "The story of Liang Shanbo and Zhu Yingtai is popularly told, but its source is unknown. Ningbo Prefectural Records, in the west of the prefectural city, there is a tomb of a virtuous woman, which says that Liang and Zhu were classmates when they were young, and Liang did not know that Zhu was a woman. Later, Liang became the magistrate of Yin, and died and was buried here. Zhu mourned at the bottom of the tomb, the tomb cracked and she died, and they were buried together. Xie An requested that they be titled the Tomb of the Virtuous Woman, so the matter should have been in the Eastern Jin Dynasty. The Yixing County Records has Zhu Yingtai's residence. The Jiaozhou Records of Shandong Province, a hundred miles south of the state, has Zhu Yingtai's tomb. Now, Shangyu also has Liang Shanbo's tomb, or it may be a mistake in transmission." The recorded story is generally familiar to us, and the records of location and time are particularly valuable.

Regarding legends, there is the "Diaochan" section, which quotes Bu's wife's remonstrance from the Annotations to the Records of the Three Kingdoms, suspecting that the so-called "Bu's wife" may be Diaochan. It also quotes the Huai'an Records: "Pizhou has a dressing table, in the ancient Lower Qi city, it is said that Lü Bu dismissed the concubine Diaochan and dressed up here. The ruins still exist." There is no historical evidence, and "Diaochan's name is only seen here, so the words of the legend are not without basis, but whether she was a wife or a concubine is unknown." The "Zhaojun" section is a compilation of references to the Zhaojun affair recorded in the Records of the Former Han Dynasty, the Records of the Later Han Dynasty, the Southern Xiongnu Biography, and the Miscellaneous Records of the Western Capital, with comparative research. The "Four Beauties" textual research is the most detailed:

"The Spring and Autumn Annals of Wu and Yue, King of Yue obtained the daughter of a woodcutter from Mount Luoluo, named Xi Shi and Zheng Dan, adorned them with silk and taught them how to walk and move. They practiced in Tucheng and approached the capital of Wu. After three years of learning etiquette, they silently entered Wu. The Records of Lost Things by Prince Zinian: Yue plotted to destroy Wu, and had two beauties, one named Yiguang and the other named Xiuming, to offer to Wu. So Xi Shi was originally named Yiguang, and her surname was Shi. Because she lived in the west, she was named Xi Shi. However, Mencius directly called her Xizi. The National Policy says: Mao Qiang first Shi. Mei Cheng's Seven Beginnings says: If first Shi and Yang Wen are made to wear gorgeous clothes and serve, then Xi Shi is also called first Shi. Because the first and west characters have the same mother, it is a mistake in transmission. Dongpo said: My family's old surname is Xi, which does not seem to be a mistake. Xi Shi's fate after the fall of Wu is unknown. Du Mu's poem, 'Xi Zi goes down to Gusu, a branch follows Chi Yi.' Song Zhiwen: 'One day returning to the old capital, dressed up to search for Ruoye.' Mozi said: Xi Shi's beauty was immersed, and there is no basis for it. The Spring and Autumn Annals of Wu and Yue: Xi Zi was killed after the fall of Wu. Now, outside the city of Shaoxing Prefecture, there is Xi Shi's tomb, which is likely to be true. Mencius's notes, citing the Historical Records, say: Xi Shi is a beauty from Yue. King Goujian of Yue offered her to King Fucha of Wu, who was very happy with her. Every time she went to the market, people who wanted to see her had to pay one Wen in gold. Now, the Historical Records does not have this statement. Guanzi's Small Scale article: Mao Qiang and Xi Shi are the most beautiful people in the world, and even if they are angry, they cannot be considered beautiful. Guanzi lived more than two hundred years before the King of Yue. Could it be that the ancients had this name, and the Yue woman used it, or is Guanzi a forgery? The story of Xi Shi following Chi Yi is discussed in detail in The Returning Guest's Collection of Books, The Mountain Cutting of Art Forests, The Drunken Words of Art Garden, Chen's Proper Pomegranate, and Hu's Learning Mountain, and will not be listed in detail. The 326th volume of the Taiping Guangji records that in July of the eleventh year of Liang Tianjian, Liu Dao of Pei County and his comrade Li Shiyan disrobed two people in Jingkou, one was Xi Shi and the other was Yiguang. It said that Yiguang was the daughter of the King of Yue, who was offered to Wu with Shi. Although the matter is obscene and not worth mentioning, it is enough to show that there were two people, and that Yiguang should not be called Xi Shi. It is said that Zheng Dan is Xi Shi's name. Also, Yue Jue Shu: Goujian became a subject of Wu, and his wife gave birth to a daughter in the pavilion on the road. Later, Wu was defeated, and the pavilion was named Nüyu, and Li was changed to Daughter Village. Lu Guangwei's Records of Wu Land: It is believed that the affair between Fan Li and Xi Shi is a mistake. The Han Dynasty's Records of the Southern Yue: Yuan Zhonggu was sealed as the Marquis of Yu'er Village, and the note that the word yu is sometimes written as 　 or 　 is now called Yuxi, and it is not necessarily about daughters. Xi Shi was actually born in Wu Xiao. Now, Xiaoshan has Luoluo Village. The Later Han Dynasty Book: Kuaiji Yuji is Xiaoshan, and the note that Xi Shi came from here believes that Zhuji is a mistake."

This research is very extensive. I remember that after "January 28th," many people used "Xi Shi" as a theme to write dramas and novels. The Times also published a travelogue of Zhuji, with photos of Xi Shi's relics. According to this record, it is a mistake. There is also a section on "Writing Fees," which is actually a study of "manuscript fees." "The matter of writing fees has existed since the Wei and Jin Dynasties, and flourished in the Tang Dynasty. Zhang Yanguang received a lot of rare treasures for Yao Xiang's stele, and Han Changli's carriages, horses, and music servants moved with thousands. At that time, there was the opinion of digging gold from the tomb. After that, drafting decrees to remove officials, from the advisory officials to the serving officials, all had writing fees. During the reign of Emperor Taizong of the Song Dynasty, writing fee money was established, and several edicts were issued to engrave stones in the Shereen Academy. Every time an official was removed, a document was sent to supervise it. Officials in the academy, down to the clerks and yamen runners, all shared the benefits. Later, those who missed the deadline would send the courtyard's children to the door to urge them to collect it. Those who were simple and sent them were not surprised. In the early years of the dynasty, this was unheard of. In recent times, those who directly drafted edicts have a slight reward, and the Beijing officials do not accept more than two coins. The regular officials in the outer prefectures and counties gradually have fixed quotas, but no one has heard of them praising them. In normal times, begging for articles is even simpler. The inscriptions on monuments and steles have begun to hear of regular thrift, which is very different from the Tang and Song Dynasties." The living conditions of selling manuscripts in ancient times can be seen. After the Ming Dynasty, I don't know if anyone has studied it.

I have extracted several things about novels on the right for novel researchers to choose from. And the contents of "Cha'an Short Stories" can also be seen in general. Such a special work can be said to be extremely extensive. What he said about spending forty years to complete the manuscript is probably the real situation. I am very clear that Da Jie can find a way to punctuate and reprint it. This book is rare, and its academic relevance should not be small.

A-Jin's Family is Sick 188

— Zhu Jiaoyang

A-Jin's whole family went to the fields to plant rice seedlings, weed, and operate the waterwheel to draw water. A newborn baby was placed steadily on the edge of the field, baked by the scorching sunlight, blown by the wild wind, and the yellow and thin face had no trace of blood.

They had no cattle, no water-drawing machine, so people became cattle and machines; when their strength was not enough, they did it desperately. When they were thirsty, they drank the muddy cold water from the river, and casually bit into rotten peaches bought from the street. They didn't think of going to the pawnshop, or borrowing money from people at high interest rates, and their lives were still stable.

They worked desperately planting rice seedlings, weeding, and drawing water. Their skin was scorched black, and they were sweating stinky all day long. At night, they slept in a musty, damp thatched hut, naked, with two or three people sleeping together on a broken door used as a bed, without a blanket to cover them. Mosquitoes came in droves to bite them. A-Jin's family, who were exhausted from working during the day, fell into a deep sleep, as if they were dead. When dawn came, their lower limbs felt heavy, like feet cast in lead, a sign of illness.

A-Jin woke up, looking at the pale sky, with no sign of rain. He forced himself to call out to his old mother, wife, and children, and the whole family went to the fields to work.

Planting, weeding, drawing water, without any movement.

The sun shone directly on their bodies, and dirt oozed out from their pores, and they became more energetic as they worked, and the symptoms disappeared.

They did this every day, and their bodies were very healthy!

The danger of drought was already in the imagination of A-Jin's family, especially A-Jin himself was very anxious.

But hope came! The sky gradually became overcast, and soon it rained, and even more rain than they needed. They were extremely happy, and the whole family rested comfortably.

The sound of rain was gurgling, and it couldn't stop. A-Jin seemed to be suffering from insomnia at night, and couldn't sleep. He was thinking about tomorrow's work and recreation. He thought until dawn and came to a decision:

Go to town to mess around for a day!

After eating rice porridge, A-Jin took his ten-year-old child, each wearing a raincoat, and撐ed a boat. In the boat were two stone of white rice and two water chestnut harvesting buckets. They braved the rain and paddled straight to town.

A-Jin carried the rice and water chestnut harvesting buckets into the pawnshop, and the two stone of rice and water chestnut harvesting buckets were pawned for more than ten yuan in total. He hurriedly took his child into a small restaurant and enjoyed a hearty meal of wine, meat, and rice.

There was nothing to do in the afternoon, so A-Jin and his child stepped into Lao Jiang's house to play cards for entertainment. His child stood beside him, urging him to go back. In half a day, the money pawned, except for a lunch that seemed like a free meal, the rest of the money was entered into other people's pockets by A-Jin, who was dominated by this poor luck. Fortunately, there was still a roll of copper coins left.

A-Jin blankly led his child out of Lao Jiang's gate, his thoughts spinning like a windmill, with 横字 blocking his head, thinking of trying to win back if he had a chance. He walked all the way to the fruit stall and bought a basket of rotten peaches with this roll of copper coins, preparing to trick his old mother and wife.

The rain was still falling, and A-Jin and his son returned to Lao Jiang's house. Lao Jiang warmly invited them to eat dinner.

Lao Jiang's wife first arranged for A-Jin's child to sleep. Lao Jiang invited three people and A-Jin to continue playing cards among the partners who came in and out. Lao Jiang lent A-Jin his gambling money.

All night long, the winners were excited and didn't mind not sleeping. But the losers couldn't sleep even if they wanted to. People who neither won nor lost were still calm and already felt a little tired. A-Jin was a loser. He smoked a water pipe and sighed, watching the winners go out to drink morning tea and the people who neither won nor lost go home to sleep.

A-Jin returned home and didn't say a word all day, just sighed coldly. His old mother and wife had already understood his problem, and they swallowed their anger and only cared about eating the rotten peaches with the children. Not eating was foolish, and the peaches seemed to have been snatched.

The sky cleared up, and A-Jin's family was indeed sick and unable to go to the fields.

Loneliness 189

— Juan Shi

I was just about to pick up my pen, preparing to write something on this paper, when suddenly a bat-like gust of wind flew in through the window, blowing the paper up, onto the teacup, the table, the bed, and finally onto the floor. During the paper's drifting, I didn't offer any assistance. If it could speak, it would probably express its resentment with more than a dozen exclamation marks, like our artists do! Now it lies quietly under my wrist, waiting for the black pen tip to smear some unknowable words on its face. Originally devoid of thoughts, I was stirred by the extraordinary experience of this piece of paper, prompting some feelings. It's not about thinking about my years of wandering, nor do I want to curse the irresistible fate that is disbelieved by most people. I am pondering: if by chance the wind hadn't blown into the room, or if it had blown in but the paper hadn't fallen to the ground, then this small square would now be filled with many other words, wouldn't it? This thought is so peculiar that it caused the hand holding the pen to tremble gradually, and finally, two lines of a smile that was not a smile formed on my cheek.

Just a minute or two ago, I was still propping up my chin, staring intently, pondering some literary problems; but now, what meanders into my mind instead is a kind of loneliness and melancholy tinged with nihilism, which makes me want to put down my pen.

No matter how much someone welcomes liveliness, there will always be an opportunity in their life when they feel the heavy burden of loneliness. It may sound a bit ridiculous, but it's as ordinary as many things in the world. A few drops of plum rain falling when the sun is shining, or hearing the sobbing of a merchant's wife during a lavish feast, often evokes a very bland feeling, which is truly a surprising discovery. As for myself, I sometimes laugh aimlessly with my mouth open, but when the feast is over and I'm alone in my small room, a wave of desolation, I don’t know where it came from, slowly grows in my heart. Dusk, late night, the faint morning light, and quiet, deserted midday are all times when I feel desolation. Loneliness is an incredible phantom, its arrival is silent, its departure is without a trace. Often, just as I pick up my pen, just as I open a book that looks solemn and prepare to start reading, just as I want to reach out and turn on the dim lamp, just as I am inspired by the charming colors of spring flowers and grasses, somehow, on my heart under my shirt, a layer of cloudy shadows, like silk or mist, has already heavily covered it. I want to tear it away, but I can't. If I let it go, the situation is truly difficult to bear. So I sink downwards, head heavy and feet light, until you begin to realize that you are lonely and prepare to try to capture its entire form for a detailed examination, it often slips away like a wisp of smoke. Then you will suddenly realize and say: Hey! It's just a dream!

Dream! That's right! In loneliness, we think of things that are distant from us, which is no different from sleepwalking. I remember that the first time I experienced the taste of loneliness was one evening when I was still living in Beiping—which was then still called Beijing. I was less than ten years old, standing at the foot of the imperial city wall, which was covered with moss and withered grass, gazing at the setting sun, which was getting bigger and bigger, redder and redder, and finally disappeared into the gray tiles of the residential houses. Several sounds of desolate bugles floated up from the foot of the city, and then the sky gradually darkened, darkened. Thousands upon thousands of crows returning to their nests circled above my head, but I still stood motionless. Gradually, I saw rickshaws disappearing, I saw a hunched man walking out of the dusk, coughing, climbing the ladder to light the triangular oil lamps on the street walls, and then I thought about going back. In that instant, a feeling of indescribable sorrow and loneliness suddenly arose in my young heart. I didn't know how to get rid of the time that followed.

In recent years, because of the busyness of life, there are generally fewer times of loneliness. Even if there are, they are like a deserted temple, without any elegant music of bells and chimes, and with few flourishing flowers and trees, losing the poetic charm of the past. Now I am facing the not-very-bright desk lamp, and the sounds of the city climb into my window over the roofs of neighboring houses. My mind is very clear. I am eager to use sweat to heal myself and slowly distance myself from loneliness.

College Days (22) 190

— Written by German Storm, translated by Chen Yinzhi

Later, when the carousel was set up again at the time of the Michael Festival, I hoped to meet her once more. Every night as soon as it got dark, I would go to that square, which greatly annoyed my friend Fritz, because I would always make excuses for being late to dinner. But among the girls riding the carousel, I never saw that slender, brown-haired girl; she was the reason I came. I walked alone through the dark paths in the palace gardens, pensively savoring the memories of that fleeting happiness.

This matter suddenly came to an end: At the beginning of winter that year, I followed my father's wishes and left the liberal arts middle school in this city to study at a science-oriented middle school in central Germany, as preparation for entering university. —Is my butterfly net still hanging on that flowering tree near the wasteland? —I don't know; I never went there again; and I still haven't caught that wooden butterfly to this day.

Several years have passed since then.

That year, after graduating from that collegiate school, I returned to my hometown for a few weeks in early autumn. Among my old friends, only Christoph was left in the old nest; the rest, including Fritz, had flown elsewhere; they were either living the interesting life of a university student, or going overseas to make a living, or sitting in the dark accounting room of some merchant house, in short, going to the places they had chosen or that fate had led them. Even Christoph had grown into a short, stout, and handsome man, and was preparing to leave his hometown, because he had been promoted from apprentice to journeyman and had to travel. But the two of us had to work together one last time in his father's workshop, and the snuffbox that had followed me during my university days was the result of this work. —My mother told me that the sturdy Mrs. Politz had suddenly died a year ago, and her daughter had soon moved to the small city where the state university was located to live with an unmarried old aunt! According to regulations, this old maid was the sole heir to her small fortune. The small house with the linden tree in front was sold by relatives after her death to pay off debts; the French tailor now had to work as a clerk in another tailor shop to make a living. One Sunday afternoon, I met him on the corner of the churchyard, where he was sitting on a bench. The skin on his prominent cheekbones was even yellower, and his black hair had turned completely gray; he was coughing, and the sun seemed to make him feel comfortable. "Ah, Mr. Philip—" he called out, recognizing me, and extended two fingers of his thin hand to me, while the rest of his fingers tightly grasped that familiar porcelain snuffbox. "Those times, ah—things aren't like those times now, Mr. Philip!" he sighed and went on. "The old woman took her household to that black cross over there; as for the girl, Nari—" he choked a few times and poured out a large pile of snuff—"you've probably heard about it!—She didn't want to, she didn't want to leave her poor father to live alone, I had to push her hand away with force. What else could I do! Children should walk their own paths to happiness!" He lowered his head and placed his hands lazily on his knees. "I want to show you the letter she wrote!—" he said after a while, "—you can see that she is very learned! She writes beautifully, and the words she uses are very lovely; a duchess couldn't write better."

Gonorrhea 192

— Dr. Cui Fuqing

This disease is related to unclean intercourse. Two days or a week later, when urinating, one feels itching, burning, and pain. A discharge or pus is initially seen at the urethral opening. The source of the disease is the invasion of the urethra by gonococcus. Now, I will analyze its structure as follows:

(1) Acute anterior urethral gonorrhea: There is a large amount of pus discharge from the urethra, severe pain during urination, occasional swelling of the penis, and pain during nighttime erections. It is also accompanied by complications of inguinal lymphadenitis and inflammation of the dorsal lymphatic vessels of the penis. After about three weeks, the pain decreases, and the pus discharge gradually reduces.

(2) Acute posterior urethral gonorrhea: It moves from the anterior urethra to the posterior urethra. When urinating, there is severe pain in the perineum, and there are drops of blood at the end of urination. Blood is also mixed in the urine. For differentiation, use two glass cups. The patient urinates half of the urine into the first cup, and then urinates the other half into the second cup. If the first cup is cloudy and the second cup is clear, this is anterior urethritis. If the first cup is thick and cloudy, and the second cup is slightly thinner and cloudy, this is posterior urethritis.

In many cases, anterior and posterior urethral gonorrhea, during treatment, turns into chronic anterior and posterior urethral gonorrhea. In the morning, there is a mucus-like substance sealing the urethral opening, and other severe pain symptoms disappear. There are a few gonorrhea threads remaining in the clear urine. For differentiation, prepare two cups as described above, and it will become clear. For oral medication for this disease, the best is "Mie Sha Lin" produced by Mei Ling Foreign Company. For topical external medication, the best is German Man Er Zhi mixed gonorrhea vaccine Gonorrhea Soother. Both of these drugs are sold by Ren Shou Western Medicine Store, No. 1 Lao De Hang Lane, Mintiniyin Road, Ba Xian Qiao, French Concession, Shanghai. The former is 1 yuan per pot, and the latter is 2.5 yuan per can, plus 1 yuan for postage.

On Gonorrhea in Women 195

— Dr. Liu Xuannu

Gonorrhea in women is caused by unclean intercourse and is divided into acute and chronic types. Proportionally, gonorrhea is more common in women than in men, and its treatment is not as easy as in men. In the early stages of infection, the vulva is slightly red and swollen, and a large amount of pus-like secretions are discharged from the vaginal opening and urethra. This type of inflammation can also affect the cervix and invade the uterus, harming the ovaries and fallopian tubes, or it can enter the bladder from the urethra, causing inflammation of the ureters and kidneys. If acute gonorrhea is not treated in time, it quickly turns into chronic gonorrhea. The vulva, labia majora, and labia minora are red and swollen, and urination feels hot and painful. Severe cases cause frequent urination (the urge to urinate frequently), or it can invade the cervix and uterine cavity, causing soreness in the lower back and a feeling of tenderness. Acute gonorrhea can even cause chills, fever, and pain. In chronic gonorrhea, all kinds of inflammation disappear, and it enters the latent period. However, during intercourse or menstruation, the secretions increase slightly. As a result, gonorrhea often induces ovaritis and peritonitis, which can be fatal. Also, due to the downward flow of secretions or the rubbing of menstrual belts and underpants, gonococci can enter the anus, causing anal gonorrhea. Its treatment requires a specialist doctor to use appropriate surgery to wash the vaginal canal and uterus, and then supplement it with effective drugs, plus self-cultivation, to have hope of recovery. The most difficult thing is to abstain from sexual intercourse. Treatment for both parties can obtain the hope of complete eradication, otherwise, this decreases and that increases, and they will never be able to leave the sea of suffering.

Talks

Mr. A-Wang's Painful Conversation 199

— Qiong Sheng

Recently, the dispute between Italy and Abyssinia over Italy's attempt to conquer Abyssinia has become increasingly urgent. Italian troops are constantly being transported to African colonies, and Abyssinia is also training its troops and preparing for war for the independence and survival of its nation. Given this tense situation, if the League of Nations truly advocates justice and righteousness, the central issue should naturally be how to immediately stop Italy's aggressive ambitions and restrain them with effective measures. However, it turns a deaf ear and pretends to be mute, just carrying on with mediation and arbitration, going through the motions.

Of course, the League of Nations has its own reasons for its understated mediation and arbitration. The reason is that this difficult problem that is not easy to solve is left to the behind-the-scenes bosses to negotiate directly, either to divide the spoils or to break up, without the League of Nations having to pay attention to it. Recently, Eden's "despair" after his visit to Rome, as well as the widely rumored breakup of the Anglo-French-Italian united front, are the result of these leading jing-speakers being unable to divide the loot equally. Therefore, the news from London says: The powers are willing to divide Abyssinia, with a part of it becoming an Italian protectorate, or Abyssinia being divided into several spheres of influence, but Italy is unwilling to accept any conditions for a peaceful solution (a dispatch from the 1st).

The business principles of imperialist haggling have their own goals in the same bed but different dreams. Although they are dissatisfied with Italy's sole appropriation, in terms of the overall interests of imperialism, they absolutely do not want Abyssinia to truly become a reality of national independence and liberation. Therefore, amid the voices of "peace" from various countries, there has been a cessation of arms shipments to Abyssinia. However, Abyssinia's Chief of Staff Lu Chang issued a statement saying: Can anyone point out where Abyssinia has not fulfilled its obligations as a member of the League of Nations? Even if the civilized countries cannot prevent the war, at least they should not prevent Abyssinia from purchasing self-defense tools. If the Italo-Abyssinian war breaks out, even if there is only one person and one gun left, they will persevere to the end. The future success or failure of Abyssinia can be put aside for the moment, but such a strong and courageous spirit is already admirable.

Passing He Kou 200

—Laoxin

Every time I go upstream on the West River, I always pass through this small town of He Kou. Because I've been there so many times, I've gradually become familiar with it.

Sometimes, because the boat doesn't necessarily arrive right away when the train does, there are many times when I have a short stay in this small town. This is not just how I have become familiar with this small town; almost everyone who travels this waterway of the West River is familiar with this small town. By the same token, this small town is also prosperous because of the comings and goings of us travelers.

The West River is a famously wild river, and it often floods wildly. Almost every year when the river rises, it goes wild, stirring up endless storms and destroying the small towns along the river. He Kou is naturally no exception. However, precisely because the West River is a wild river and people are afraid of it, the route from Guangzhou to He Kou has been changed to land and switched to trains. That quickly made this unknown small town prosperous, because after everyone changed to land routes, He Kou became an essential transit station.

When you come out of the 'Guangsan Train,' following the road from the station, without any doubt, just keep walking, and you will reach the shore where the boats are docked. Along the way, you will be surprised by the countless women, using their uniquely sharp and delicate voices, calling out to you:

"Sir, Zhaoqing ferry! It's about to leave."

"Going to Wuzhou, the ×× Fast Ferry is about to depart."

"Sir, barge!..."

This chorus of voices will penetrate your ears. If you are quick, you can call one of them and agree to have them transport you in their boat to the Wuzhou boat or barge anchored on the water. You can hand over your luggage to them without any effort on your part. If you are a seasoned traveler on this waterway, you can just walk straight to the shore. Anyway, they won't rob you of your belongings; they are just working to make a living. People who are new to Guangdong will definitely find them strange, because they are one of the savage races, as the great Dr. Hu Shi said. According to countless anthropological studies, they are all pure savages. They live on the sea, and their home is a small boat with a canopy. Their name, in academic terms, is "Dan people," but we call them "Dan family girls." They, like the dock coolies, use their physical strength to earn money.

The small town of He Kou belongs to Sanshui County. Because it is relatively well-known, many people mistakenly believe it is the county seat of Sanshui, but in fact, the county seat of Sanshui is still at Lubao across the sea. There are countless food shops here, probably because their purpose is primarily to serve travelers, so they are all simple but complete. Every time I come from Guangzhou or return from Zhaoqing, I always stay here for a while.

Last year, after the West River rose, I went from Guangzhou to Guangning again. When I got off the 'Guangsan Train,' I felt something was different. Not only were there fewer "Dan family girls," but the place was also much more desolate. Therefore, as I walked out of the station, I kept wondering, looking at the traces of erosion caused by the floodwater at the station, and I felt a sense of infinite regret. When I got to the shore, I still followed the old routine and sat at Li Xiuji's fish congee shop to eat something.

"Why, it seems much more deserted this year?"

I asked the waiters with a questioning tone. They replied:

"Well, the rotten ×'s stinky water flooded us for ten or eight days. Of course it's deserted. We're lucky to be able to reopen our shop. Many Dan family girls don't want to come back from Zhaoqing. It's like this every year, it's really hopeless!..."

I left this small town, which had lost its vitality, with a sense of sadness.

This year, I have no chance to travel this waterway again. Now, from this big city five days away by water, I see news again about the wild West River flooding, and I can't help but think of this small town that has not yet recovered its vitality. When I think about it in the quiet night, I also murmur:

"It's like this every year, it's really hopeless!"

Tiger Head 201

— Bina

Five-year-old Xiao Xiao lay on the grass, gazing at the sky in a daze. A few white clouds were slowly moving in the wind.

"Brother, what do you think that looks like?" she said.

Seven-year-old Pei Pei looked up and said, "It looks like a tiger's head. Look how big that curved mouth is!"

"Brother, look, next to it, the pointy shape looks like a woman's face."

"It looks like sister's face, she even has a perm."

Just then, a gust of wind came, and the white cloud that resembled a tiger's head scattered the shape of the woman's face.

"Ah! Sister has been swallowed by the tiger!" Pei Pei clapped his hands and said.

Xiao Xiao didn't say a word, just kept looking at the sky, and suddenly, she burst into tears.

Pei Pei was stunned and said, "Sister, why?"

Xiao Xiao could only cry, her mouth wide open; tears dripped onto the grass.

Pei Pei panicked, looking at his wooden horse, as if he wanted the

Page 20

wooden horse to answer his question.

"Sister, do you want my ball?"

Sister shook her head, her hair all damp with tears.

Pei Pei was confused; he stared at his sister with wide eyes. After a long time, Pei Pei's tears involuntarily fell on his sister's face, but he didn't know why he was crying.

"Did Pei Pei upset his sister again?"

Mom heard the crying and rushed out of the house.

Sister didn't care that she was barefoot, she ran straight to her mother; she grabbed her mother's clothes and said, "Mom... Mom, Sister... was... swallowed... by the tiger!" As she spoke, she pointed to the sky with her little finger.

Mom laughed.

"Who said that?"

"Brother said it."

"Pei Pei, why are you teasing your sister?"

"I didn't tease her. There was a cloud that looked like a tiger's head, and another cloud that looked like sister's face. Then the tiger's head scattered sister's face. So I said, 'Sister was swallowed by the tiger.' That's why sister cried," Pei Pei said, clapping his little hands and laughing.

"Xiao Xiao, be good, don't cry, sister is fine in the house."

Xiao Xiao didn't believe her, tears still falling from her face.

"Look, isn't that sister coming?" Pei Pei said, jumping up and down.

Xiao Xiao struggled out of her mother's arms, stumbled and ran to meet her sister.

"Sister, you weren't dragged away by the tiger?"

Sister didn't understand her words; she only asked, "Xiao Xiao, why are you crying like this?"

Mother told her everything, and sister felt as if that tiger's head was really going to devour her, and she wanted to cry too.

Movie News

Anecdotes Welcoming Zhou and Hu's Return to China 206

It's hard for Mr. Zhou and Ms. Hu

When the McKinley arrived at the Jianghaiguan Wharf, the shore was full of cars and people. As soon as they stepped onto the shore, they were busy nodding and shaking hands, simply overwhelmed; the general reporters were busy taking pictures, interviewing, and requesting interviews; the crowd of people squeezed them so tightly that it was difficult to move, and Mr. Zhou and his wife and Ms. Hu were covered in sweat.

Mr. Zhou Jianyun at the Welcome Meeting

Zhou and Hu returned to China. On the afternoon of the 8th, at 2 o'clock, all the colleagues of the Star Company held a meeting to welcome them. Mr. Zhou stood up and reported everything he had seen and heard abroad. He was passionate and impassioned when it was painful, and made people smile knowingly when it was humorous. In a continuous speech of more than two hours, he reported on their experiences in the Soviet Union and Europe, and talked about the current political situation, customs, and feelings of various countries that Zhou had seen and heard during his travels. His mouth was like a hanging river, endless; and every sentence and word could shake people's hearts. In such a long time, not only was Mr. Zhou's spirit not tired at all, but all the listeners were also very inspired and moved. Mr. Zhou is not only a shrewd, capable, and powerful film entrepreneur, but also a talented speaker.

Hu Die in the Mouth of Old Master Zheng

At the welcome meeting, Mr. Zhou Jianyun reported on Ms. Hu Die. Her Mandarin is very good, her attitude is very calm, and her words are very humble. At the end, he said: This time abroad, I have not made the progress that everyone expected, and I am very ashamed. I hope that my comrades will not hesitate to guide me, so that I can work harder and move towards the road to success. Later, Old Master Na introduced in public, saying: "Miss Hu is really too modest. Aside from anything else, just take her concise report and appropriate speech just now, and compare it with her speech when she went abroad. This alone proves that she has made amazing progress."

Very Excited Zheng Zhengqiu

Old Master Zheng Zhengqiu is very thin. Everyone knows that she is a weak and frail male Lin Daiyu. She spends seven or eight days in bed out of ten. Her voice is low, and she is usually silent most of the time. But on the day Zhou and Hu returned to China, at the welcome Zhou and Hu meeting, Old Master Zheng's face was radiant, his voice was particularly loud, and his words were very humorous, which made everyone laugh at him. He himself said that his spirit was particularly excited and happy that day compared to usual.

Grabbing Bread

The welcome meeting lasted a long time. When the meeting adjourned, it was after 6 o'clock in the afternoon. Everyone's stomach seemed to be panicking. Then, a talking sound came from a corner, "What?" "Snack tickets." "Do you have one?" For a moment, everyone at the meeting got it, and in such a happy mood, everyone went to the place to collect snacks, and each hand exchanged a snack coupon for a package of bread and cake, and immediately began to munch on it.

"Selling Smiles" 207

—Great Shanghai Reflection

"Crazy Night of Wind and Rain" is the first thunder prepared by the Jinan Company after its reopening. The play has a profound meaning, directed by Feng Ting and written by his younger brother Feng Yiwei. The Kun brothers are both young and handsome, and their thoughts are intelligent, but whether they will succeed is still unpredictable.
